Now that I have completed for you, O sons, this book, which is the final part of medical science with its completion, and have reached the end in it, through its explanations and declarations, it seemed good to me to complete it for you with this Treatise which is a part of practice, that is, surgery with the hand.
Since the operation with the hand has fallen into disuse in our region and during our time entirely: until perhaps its knowledge perished, and its trace was cut off: and nothing remained of it except small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which were altered by hands: and they fell into error and hesitation, until its intentions were closed, and its power was lost: It seemed good to me to revive it with the order of this Treatise according to the method of positioning, declaration, and abbreviation: and to come with forms of cautery tools and other instruments of work: which is made by addition of declarations, and by hastening what is necessary.
The reason why a good practitioner of it with his hand is not found in our time is: because the art of medicine is long, and its author must be trained beforehand in the science of anatomy, as Galen narrated, until he knows the benefits of the members, and their forms, and their conjunction and separation, and has knowledge of bones, nerves, tendons, and their number, and their emergence, and of pulsating and quiet veins, and the exits of those places.
And because of this, Hippocrates said that the name is abundant with the name, but scarce with the work, and especially in the art of the hand.
We have already spoken of this at the beginning of this book.
For he who is not knowledgeable about what we have said concerning anatomy will not be able to avoid falling into error, by which people are killed: as I have seen many of those who are formed from this science, and who boast about it without knowledge and without experience.
This is because I saw a foolish doctor cut into a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck, and he cut certain arteries in the neck: therefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead under his hands.
And I saw another doctor who attempted to extract a stone from an elderly man, and the stone was large. He therefore proceeded to do so and extracted it along with a piece of the bladder. Therefore, the man died on the third day.
And I had indeed been called to extract it: and I saw that because of the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, he would die.
And I saw another doctor who was receiving payment from one of the Dukes in our land for his medical services: and it happened that a black eunuch who was with him broke his leg near the heel. The doctor, acting with his ignorance, quickly bound the fracture over the wound with cushions and tight wooden splints, and did not allow the injury to breathe.
Then he finished treating him according to his own desires. Then he left him for several days and instructed him not to loosen the bandage: and he remained thus until his leg became abscessed, and his foot as well, and it led to their destruction.
I was summoned therefore to him: and I hurried to loosen the bandage: and peace followed, and he escaped from his pains.
However, the corruption was already confirmed in the member: and I could not restrain it.
Let corruption cease to spread in the member until it perishes.
And I saw another doctor who punctured the cancerous abscess: and it became ulcerated after days, until its malice was magnified with its lord.
Which means that when the cancer is purely from a melancholic humor, then it should not be approached with iron at all, unless it is in a limb that can tolerate being entirely cut off.
And for this reason, O sons, it is necessary for you to know that the operation with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, the operation which is associated with safety: and the operation, with which there is danger in most dispositions.
And I have already alerted in every part of this book where the operation comes that is filled with fear and dread.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to beware of it and abandon it: so that fools do not find a way to speak about it and dishonor it.
Take therefore the measure with care and protection, and tend to your patients with ease and firmness, and make use of the better way leading through God's grace to salvation and a praiseworthy succession: and leave behind terrible diseases difficult to heal: and remove from yourselves that which causes you fear, so that hesitation may not enter upon you in your faith and comfort.
For it remains more to your glory, and higher in this world, and finally to your quantities.
For Galen has already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat bad illness: lest you be called bad doctors.
Now I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
First Chapter.
About the Hot Cauterization and Sharp Medicinal Cauterization, categorized and ordered from head to foot, with forms of instruments and cauterizing tools: and everything necessary for the procedure.
Second Chapter.
About cutting and piercing, bloodletting and venting, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and similar procedures: all categorized and ordered with forms of instruments.
Third Chapter.
About restoration, dislocation, and treatment of twisting, and similar procedures: categorized and ordered from head to foot, with forms of instruments.
But before I recall the procedure with it, I must say what its benefits are and what harms it has: and in what complexion it is administered.
I say therefore that the discourse on the quality of the benefit of the cautery and its harm is a lengthy and subtle matter of knowledge and an hidden secret.
Also, many wise people have spoken about it and disagreed on it: and for me, a little of their discourse is sufficient, fearing lengthiness.
I say therefore that the cautery is beneficial universally to all complexions that have matter and those without matter: except for two complexions, which are the hot complexion without matter, and the dry complexion without matter.
In the hot and dry complexion with matter, they disagreed. For some said that the cautery is beneficial in it. And others said the opposite of that, namely that the cautery is not suitable for the disease which arises from heat and dryness: because the nature of fire is heat: and it is inappropriate to be cured from a hot and dry illness with something hot and dry.
And he who says the opposite said that through the cautery there is benefit in every hot and dry disease which occurs in human bodies: because when you compare the body of a man and its moistures to the temperament of fire, you find the body of a man to be cold.
And indeed I say through his words: because from the experiment it has already revealed to me that many times.
However, it should not come to that unless one who has already been tested and trained in the chapter on the last exercise of cauterization, and known the diversity of human complexions, and the disposition of diseases in themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and the duration of them.
From the other complexions there is no fear for you: especially in cold and moist diseases. For indeed all doctors have agreed on these: and they have not disagreed about treating them with cauterization.
And know, sons, that from the secret of healing with cauterization by fire, and its goodness over cauterization with burning medicine is this: for fire is simple, whose action does not reach beyond the part that is cauterized: and it does not harm another connected part except with a slight damage.
The action of burning medicine reaches to that which is distant from the parts: and it may cause disease in a part that is difficult to heal, and it may even kill.
But fire, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not cause that, unless there is an excess.
Now this has become known to us through experience, because of the length of service and study with the art, and standing on the truth of things: and because of this, I am excused for the length of the speech.
And if it were not, because it is not permitted to this my book to bring you the hidden secret in fire, and the nature of its operation in the bodies of its expulsion, by which it expels diseases demonstrated philosophically, which would be sharpened by your minds.
And know, sons, that they disagree on the time when the cautery should be done, and they place the better time in spring.
And I say that cautery is suitable at all times: because the harm caused by the time is overshadowed by the benefit that is drawn with the cautery. And especially if the cautery is for pains caused by necessary, strong, urgent pains that do not tolerate delay: because it is feared that a greater harm may occur than the small damage that temporarily intervenes due to the time.
And let it not fall into your minds, o sons, that which is not feared except by the common people and foolish doctors, namely that there is not always a return of that disease which is cured by cautery: and they put forward this consequence, and things are not as they think: because cautery is only in place of medicine which alters the temperament and dries up the moistures which are the cause why pains occur.
However, cautery exceeds medicine by the speed of its recovery and the power of its operation, and the strength of its dominance: and it is possible for the disease to return at some time according to the temperament of the patient and the location of his disease and its power: and what is prepared in his body by the aggregation of superfluities in him: and what comes to him in acquiring from foods and similar things due to those causes, unless the disease is such that cautery is administered.
A subtle illness in the limb of few excesses and moistures, like a tooth cauterization, because of pain, and similar to it, for it is possible that that pain does not return in it. But that happens in few cases.
But the common saying again, that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, is a true statement: not in regard to what they aim at in it: for they believe that there is no cure which compares with medicine, nor with anything else after the failure of cauterization.
The matter is contrary to that, and the intent, which states that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, is not so, except when we administer modes of cure in some illnesses, and those medicines do not help: then we apply cauterization at the end, and it helps: thus it follows that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the understanding of the common people and many foolish doctors.
The ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron: and they did not say this except because of the equality of gold and the subtlety of its substance: and they said that the site of the cauterization does not produce pus. But that is not absolutely true: for I have already tested it and found that it does not cause that effect in some bodies without other factors.
And cauterization with it is good and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you ignite cauterization with gold in fire, it is not clear to you when it is ignited according to the amount you want, because of the redness of the gold: and when it quickly cools down, and if you add more heat to it, it melts in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the artisan falls from that into the task: and because of this, the Cauterization with iron is done more quickly and closer to us, from straightness to the operation.
And indeed I have already arranged this Chapter on Cauterization according to the chapters: and I have ordered them from head to foot: so that it may help the seeker find what they want from it.
Chapter II.
Here, cauterization is applied to the dominance of moisture and cold over the brain: these two are the causes of phlegm, and the abundance of fluid flow from the head to the regions of the eyes and ears, and an abundance of sleep, and tooth pain, and throat pain: and universally all illnesses that occur due to cold, such as paralysis, phlegm, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar ailments.
The method of cauterization is that you instruct the patient to purge first with cleansing and dissolving medicine for three nights or four, according to what the strength of the patient, their age, and their habit require.
Then instruct him to shave his head with a novacula. Then have him sit between your hands in a square position, so that he has placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the tip of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever therefore your middle finger reaches, mark that place with ink.
Then cauterize with olive oil fire: whose form is this.
Then place it on the marked spot with ink, by the descent by which your hand is gradually tightened, and you will rotate it. Then quickly remove your hand, and look at the place.
If you see that the amount of alkali or the amount of zehreb has been exposed from the bone, then raise your hand. And if not, apply your hand with the same iron, or with another one if it cools down: until the bones appear, which I have told you about.
Then take something from salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak the cloth in it, and place it on the spot: and leave it for three days.
Then place on it a cloth soaked in butter, and leave it on the spot until the burn scab is dissolved. Then treat it with the ointment tetrapharmacon until it heals.
They have said that the longer the wound remains open, it expels pus: therefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized down to the bone: and the cautery should be held until something of the density of the bone is burned.
Then it is scraped after that which was burned from the bone, then it should be treated.
And others say that it is necessary to use the cautery until it makes a deep impression on the bone so that the bone falls out, which becomes like the shape of a key: or an instrument which women place with a small amount of alphabet poured in: and they claim that vapors of the head escape from this location, and the wound should be left open for a long time.
Then it should be treated until it is stabilized.
To me, these two types of cautery do not seem to work at all except in certain people according to a method of fear.
And to leave it, in my opinion, is better for its safety.
For the head is weakened by the breaking of its natural continuity: as we have testified in other members: and especially when the head of the patient is weak by nature: and indeed the first type of cautery is safer and better for me, and I use it: therefore act with it for safety.
Chapter III.
When chronic pain occurs throughout the entire head and persists in the patient, they use hirers, cochiis, head purges, oils, and emplasteries. And especially if it has already been cauterized with the cautery we mentioned and it does not benefit from those treatments: then consider. For if the head of the sick person is strong in its natural constitution and not weak, and finds intense cold: then cauterize with another cautery a little under it. Then cauterize the entire horn of his head with a cautery, so that it does not penetrate the skin, and uncover from the bone the amount we have mentioned. And cauterize it with one cautery on the back of his head, in the place which is called the vase: and it is the place where the cupping vessel is placed: and raise your hand here, and do not uncover the bone. For the sick person finds because of that a very severe pain, and different from the pain of all the other head cauterizations.
And I say this is the Cautery in its place: and it must be a cautery with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of the head more finely than the cautery with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When pain and swelling occur in part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and it is purged with cleansing medicines for the head, and the remaining treatment, which I mentioned in the divisions of diseases, does not help: then cauterization should be performed in two ways: either with a sharp burning medicine, or with iron.
The cautery with sharp and burning medicine is such that you take one garlic clove, and peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides. Then cut the painful area with a wide lancet until you make a place under the skin where the tooth is caught.
Insert it under the skin until it is hidden; then bind over it with a poultice of proper constriction, and leave it for fifteen hours, then remove it, and let the wound be open for two or three days: afterwards apply to it a cloth soaked in butter until the place produces pus: then treat it with an ointment until it heals.
And if you wish to do this with some burning medicines, which I have written about in the twelfth chapter, on burning mediines.
The cauterization of it with an iron is according to this method. A cautery with fire, whose form is this.
And it is named Clauilis: because the form of its head is like the form of a nail, in which there is something curved, and in the middle of it there is a small protrusion.
Then place it on the area and hold your hand steady: and you shall rotate the iron gradually with speed: and the amount that is burned should be according to the thickness of the skin, like its midpoint. And lift your hand so that the artery below is not burned and blood flow does not occur.
Then soak the cloth in salt water, and place it on the area, and leave it for three days: then place the cloth with butter: afterwards treat with ointment until it heals.
And if you want, cauterize this half of the head with the second knife end of the Cauterizer. And beware of incising the artery in this half of the head, not properly the old one.
On the method of cauterizing in the old half of the head.
When you treat half of the head, with what we have said from the previous treatment, and what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and if the treatment does not help: and you see from the disease that what we have said about using the first cautery with medicine, or with fire cautery, is not enough for it, then you must heat the knife cautery until it whitens after you mark the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or almost so: and withdraw your hand once, and press it until you cut the artery, and reach the bone.
However, you must be careful not to continue the cautery on the jaw that moves during chewing, so that the side or the nerve that moves it is not burned, which could cause spasms.
And be on guard and cautious about the flow of blood from the artery that has been cut. For in cutting it there is fear, especially for one who does not know what he is doing, and who is not skilled or experienced: and he leaves the operation at the very beginning.
And I will come with a recollection of the management of blood flow occurring from an artery according to its manner, and in its place in this book.
If you see from the illness that this cautery is not sufficient for it, and you see the body of the sick person tolerating the cautery in the middle of the head as we have narrated, treat the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of an artery with a cautery having two knives. For cautery is better than this and more beneficial.
Regarding the method of cauterizing for ear pain.
When pain occurs in the ear due to cold and is treated with solutions and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, and if the pain does not subside, then use fire cautery: and it is that which is called a Point, whose form is this.
Then make points with it after its ignition around the entire ear, as it revolves: or around both, if the pain is in both at the same time. And move the cautery away from the root of the ear for a moment after you have marked the places with branding: and let the quantity of the cautery be ten points on the entire ear, and about that.
Then treat the areas until they heal.
Regarding the method of cauterizing for torture.
Chapter VII.
Torture which is treated with cauterization is only of the kinds that occur from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of diseases.
And avoid cauterization in the kind that occurs from dryness and spasm of the nerve.
When you treat this kind of torture with plasters, and head purgations, and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the second a little below its temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the affected area. Because softening does not occur unless in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is to cauterize directly at the upper end of the ear under the temple a little, and another at the temple, whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until the amount equal to the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a type of knife, whose shape is as mentioned before; however, it is not as fine, as you see: and it must be a knife that is somewhat excessively thick.
Then treat the areas with what precedes: until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in old apoplexy.
When apoplexy becomes old, and you treat it with what we have said, and your medication does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on every horn of his head, and a cauterie in the middle of the head, as we have said, and a cauterie on the back of the head, according to what precedes: and the method of the cauterie should be according to what precedes.
It is also cauterized with a cautery on the mouth of the stomach: and it is the very last.
Then it should be treated with what has been mentioned previously.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in the drink given first to the patient there be hyraceum and pills that cleanse the brain.
Then shave the head of the patient entirely, and place on the back of his head a poultice of mustard as described in the chapter on poultices: and apply it several times.
This is the method of the cautery: and do it according to the same order which I said there.
If therefore he is healed by that, it is good. If not: then make three cauteries on the back part of his head, which should descend from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the eye: and place between each cautery the thickness of a finger.
Then care for the cautery with what preceded it.
If however you wish for an addition, and the patient is tolerant of it: then make a cautery in the middle. If you wish for an addition: then cauterize it over the two horns.
Then care for it until it heals: let the cautery be oiled according to the method which was mentioned.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in paralysis and softening.
Chapter Ten.
It is necessary that you proceed with the cleansing of the head with hogweed and with what we have mentioned.
Then shave the head of the patient: afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and a cautery on every horn of the head, and a cautery on its posterior, and three on the cervical vertebrae.
If however you need more than those for the sickness and softening of the body, and the patient is tolerant, and the illness is strong: then cauterize it with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and the last with a cautery until it is burned deeply from the skin, and lift your hand. Then care for it until it heals: and thus oil the cautery.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized unless his epilepsy is due to phlegm.
Therefore, you must cleanse its brain first with honey, and with the rest of the treatment we mentioned in the division: when the patient is severe, or is tolerant in receiving medicines.
If it is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargle and cleansing mastications for the brain are administered, after many days with the improvement of foods.
Then shave his head, then cauterize it with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what preceded in the method: and with another cautery on the back of his head, and on all the horn of his head with a cautery. If the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize it with the cauteries I mentioned for those having paralysis, and softening of the body over the cervical vertebrae, and dorsal vertebrae: and let it be an olive oil cautery according to the method that preceded.
If the patient is a child, then apply a fine cautery according to this method.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize it with the cauteries we mentioned for those having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess inclined towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him in drink what will cleanse his brain, according to what preceded in the division: then shave the head of the patient, and make afterwards a properly made band from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head: and the patient sitting upright shall be held on all sides.
Then apply the liniment. And it is better from old sheep's butter. And heat it over the fire with moderate heating, to a degree that can be tolerated by a finger when inserted into it. Then evacuate it in the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it cools down.
Do this for the patient once every week, along with the rest of his good regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making very many small points, except where you hold the hand with the cautery: let it be smelled.
For this type of cautery moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place on it a cloth soaked in butter or hen's fat.
About the method of cauterizing for water descending to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When the beginning of water in the eye is made clear to you by the signs which I have mentioned in the division, then begin and purify the patient, with what cleanses his head.
And keep him away from all moisture, and have him sit in a bath, on fasting for several days.
Then command him to shave his head, and cauterize it in the middle of his head. Then cauterize it over both temples with two cauteries, if the onset of water descent is in both eyes at the same time: or from one side, if the onset of water is in one eye: and sever with the cautery all veins and arteries which are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long in width across the temples: and beware of the flow of blood.
If you see anything of it, then sever it immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with the wisdom which is in the extraction of arteries, and their severing, and caution against the flow of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, below two bones, with two ultimately extended cauteries.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in ancient tears.
When the tears of the eyes are ancient, persistent: and they are over veins, and arteries which are on the exterior of the head, it is verified that this is from cold, phlegmatic excesses: then cauterize with the cautery I mentioned in the onset of descending water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries over both temples, and two cauteries on the neck below two bones. And if additional treatment is needed, then cauterize it on the entire side of the eye, over the end of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
On the method of cauterizing for nasal odor.
When you treat it with what we mentioned in the division and the treatment does not help: then hurry, and give the patient infirmocochias for three nights: then shave his head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with olive oil. Then cauterize it with a key cautery twice, above the eyebrows slightly under the hair.
And be careful of the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of the key cautery.
On the method of cauterizing for the relaxation of the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is relaxed due to illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid once with this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it slightly above the eyebrows with two cauteries on each side: and they should extend from both temples: and the length of each cautery should be according to the length of the eyebrow: and do not push your hand too much with the cautery, but according to the amount that the third eyelid is burned.
On the method of cauterizing the eyelid when the inverted hairs irritate the eye.
Cauterization is performed in two ways: either with fire; or with burning medicine.
In cauterization with fire, instruct the patient beforehand to remove his hairs, if he is one of those who shave them, until they grow out and are even. If they puncture him at their origin: then bind his eyes with a thread, so that they do not move until they heal.
When they grow out and are even, then place the patient's head in your lap: then mark above the eyelids of his eyes with a branding iron, making a mark in the shape of a myrtle leaf: and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a cloth soaked in egg white: or in psyllium mucilage over the eye.
Then cauterize with fire, the form of which is this.
Then cauterize over the figure you marked gradually in many places until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, appears properly burned all over.
And the sign of the healing of your work is: if you see the eyelid already contracting, and the hairs rising around the eye's puncture.
Therefore lift your hand then: and leave him for three days.
Then place a cloth with butter over it until the eschar is removed. Then care for it with ointment until it heals.
If any of the hairs return after an hour, and the eyelid softens: then apply the cautery again to that place as you did at first.
If the hairs are on the lower [lid]: then cauterize it until it rises to its natural position: and [make sure] it is even so that the hairs do not pierce the eye.
It is that you should advise the patient to let the hairs grow until they lengthen and even out. Make a shape of a myrtle leaf from cloth paper.
Then take from known soap and from unslaked lime one ounce each; then grind them together well, and make it quickly so that it does not cool. Then spread it over the paper you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it over the eyelid of one or both eyes. And place under the eye a cloth soaked in egg white: and let the patient's head be in your lap.
And place your index finger on the medicine and press it for a moment. And you should move it whenever the patient feels the bite of the medicine: for its bite is like fire.
Therefore, while this which he discovered as a bite persists, then discontinue the medication, and move it with your finger. Therefore, when the bite ceases, then remove the medication, and wash the eye with water.
And then consider, if you see the eyelid rise, as it rises with contraction by fire or with incision, it is good: and if not, then again apply the medication over the place where the medication does not leave a mark and does not blacken, until your operation is equalized and the eye contracts.
Then apply Cottus with butter on it until the burnt skin is removed. Then treat it with a diaphoretic ointment, or another, until it heals.
And it is necessary for you during the operation to guard with utmost care that nothing from the medication falls into the eye.
If the eyelid softens after a few days and something from hairs struggles in the eye, then apply the medication again to the place that softens from the eyelid itself, as you did at first. Then treat it until it heals.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And you should know that the eyes of humans differ in size and smallness. Therefore, let your consideration be according to this: and the way of righteousness is not hidden from one who has a zeal for this art.
On the method of cauterizing in a lacrimal fistula.
When you treat a fistula, with what we have said about the divisions of diseases, and your treatment does not help: then, you must cauterize it according to this method.
Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, and let the attendant hold his head between his hands in such a way that it does not move or jerk with his head.
Then place a cloth soaked in egg white or in psyllium mucilage over his eye: then cauterize with fire, the form of which is this.
Let it be hollow, like the form of a vulture feather quill from one end, with which the cauterization is done: and if you want it to penetrate to the other end, and if you want it to go up, try it thus.
However, this hollow one is better for your work.
Then express the fistula if it is open, and extract the pus from it, and dry it: and if it is not open, then open it and extract its pus.
Then place the cauterization tool, which is made very hot, on it.
And hold your hand near the cauterization tool by the eye, toward the nose side, so that your hand does not waver or disturb the patient: and place the cauterization tool on the fatty part of the eye and burn it.
If therefore you reach at the beginning of your cauterization up to the bone, it will be well. And if not: then repeat the cauterization once, or twice, if you need that: and leave it for three days.
Then apply the poultice with butter, and treat it with a drying ointment until it heals.
If forty days have passed and it has not healed: then apply a sharp corrosive medicine over it until the bone is exposed: and scrape it according to how it is described in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing the fistula, which some first mentioned. Attend to the location of the fistula and find it: then place a fine camahan into the fissure, that is, a fine cannula, whose form is this. And pour into it the quantity of a drachm of molten lead, and hold your hand with a good retention cane, and do not move the patient at all, so that the molten lead does not run to or reach his eye.
And it is necessary to place on the patient's eye a poultice soaked in egg white, or in water.
For the lead burns the area of the fistula and heals it with a remarkable healing.
If the fistula is healed with what we have said about cauterization and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer the nasal passage and redirect the fistula to the course of the nose, according to how it will come to its own proper place.
On the method of cauterizing in fissures of the lips.
Often fissures occur on the Lip, which are called Pili, and especially on the lips of children.
Therefore, when you treat these fissures, with what we have said in the division of diseases, and if the treatment does not help, then prepare a small knife-like cautery with fire, according to this form.
And its concavity should be according to the fineness of the knife.
Then place it, when ignited, quickly on the fissures, until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with cerote until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in oral fistulas.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth: then it produces pus and bursts: afterwards it becomes old, and pus runs, and a fistula forms: then you treat it, and if the treatment does not help, then you must heat a cautery according to its size, so that it may fit into the fistula. Then insert it, when ignited, into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its depth and bottom: do this once or twice.
Then treat it afterward with what we have said about the treatment until it is healed.
If therefore the pus is removed and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place and remove the corrupted bone according to what will come upon its head.
On the method of cauterizing in gums and softened teeth.
When the gum is softened due to moisture and the teeth are loosened, and you treat it with medicines and it does not improve: then place the patient's head in your lap.
Then with a fire cauterize it, the form of which will come after this, so that you place a cannula on the tooth: and insert into it a ignited cauterium quickly: and hold your hand for a moment, until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
And lift your hand: then repeat the cauterization several times, according to what you wish.
Then let the patient fill his mouth with salt water and hold it for one hour: and spit it out.
For the loose tooth is fixed, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
On the method of cauterizing for tooth pain.
When the pain of the tooth is due to cold, or there is cold in it, or a worm, and treatment with medicines does not help: then cauterization is applied in two ways: either cauterization with butter: or cauterization with fire.
The cautery of this is with butter, that you take cow's butter and boil it in an iron spoon, or in copper. Then take the cloth, and wrap it over the end of the bandage. Then submerge it in boiled butter: and place it on the painful tooth quickly, and hold it until it cools: then repeat it several times, until the heat penetrates to the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge wool, or cloth in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth: and place a heated iron on top of it until the heat reaches the bottom of the tooth cavity.
The cautery of this with fire is to apply a brass tube or an iron tube. And let there be something thick on the body of it so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
Then with fire cauterize it, whose form will come: and place it on that tooth: and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do this several times, for the pain will be removed, either on that same day or another day.
And it is necessary after applying that cautery that the patient fills his mouth with good butter and holds it for one hour: then spit it out.
And this is the form of the cautery.
Cauterize with whichever end you wish according to what is possible: and this is the form of the cannula.
On the method of cauterizing in strophulus.
When strophulas are caused by phlegm and cold moistures, and do not respond to digestion through medicines, and you wish for their rapid digestion: then use a concave cautery, whose form is this.
Having two open ends, so that smoke may exit at the cautery from the other end: and place it ignited upon the aposteme once, and a second time if needed, until it reaches the depth of the aposteme.
If the aposteme is small: then place the cautery according to the size of the aposteme.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it a cloth soaked in butter until what the fire has burned is removed.
Then treat it with tooth ointment until the shape of the cannula heals.
On the method of cauterizing in hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
When moistures overcome the channel of the lungs, and especially when this occurs with a cold temperament, then it is necessary that the patient be first evacuated with dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it in the no crater at the root of the throat in a depressed area: and be careful not to reach with the cautery to the throat itself, nor on the skin, except slightly.
Then cauterize it with another cautery near the joint of the neck at its last vertebra: and let the cautery be according to the method that preceded.
Then care for it with what has preceded until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in diseases of the lungs, and cough.
When cough and disease of the lungs are from cold humidities, and the patient does not have fever, nor consumption, and the disease is chronic: then cauterize it with two cauteries above the clavicle in depressed, mild, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two nipples: and let the cautery be of a tube according to the form that preceded.
And if you wish your cauterization to be done by pricking with a cautery which is called Point, whose form has preceded in the pricking of ear pain: and let the pricks be from thirty points up to about another.
Then care for it with what has preceded until it is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this form. Therefore, the cautery is alleviated when you perform three cauteries with it at once.
Chapter Twenty-Seven.
When the head of the helper is displaced due to moisture and does not return to its place at the time of its usual return from displacement, until it becomes accustomed to returning, then it is displaced by a small movement, which occurs as we have already testified, then you must restore the displacement first. Then the patient should lie on their back, or on the healthy side. Then lift the skin that is inside the Titillici upwards with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint is displaced inward.
Then take a cautery with two prongs. Its form is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates to the other side, and the figure of the cauterization will come with four cautery marks.
And sometimes the cauterization is done with a cautery having three prongs, hence the figure of the cauterization then has six marks: and the prongs are according to the fineness of the wire.
And this is the form of the cautery having three prongs.
And sometimes one is added to this manner, hence there are eight cautery marks.
Then place ground onions with salt on the cautery. Then secure the patient to stillness, so that the limb is not moved for some time until it is strengthened.
And if the displacement is upward, and this rarely occurs, then cauterize it on the shoulder with a key-shaped cautery or with multiple punctures of cauteries.
For the joint is strengthened, and the moisture is removed: and the sick person is healed.
On the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and excessive moisture occur in the stomach, causing it to deviate from its natural disposition, and phlegm increases around it, and usual methods of treatment are not beneficial: then the sick person should lie on their back, extend their legs, and hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, a cautery under the spoon-shaped area of the chest the size of one finger with a key-shaped cautery, and two cauteries below from both sides of one cautery, until the shape of the cauteries forms a triangle. And space them apart so they do not join, when they would form pus.
And the depth of the cautery should be two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
And the shape of the cauteries should follow this form without addition: and if you wish, cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery with which this cautery is made be one according to the shape of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by marking the area to be treated with this cautery: and it is done by marking a point on the stomach according to the size you wish with encaustic; then cauterize it with a point cautery; then treat it with the preceding method of treatment until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing the cold spleen.
When there occurs in the spleen pain from cold and moisture, or from thick wind, until it departs from its natural complexion by expelling excess, and the patient is treated with what we have said, but does not improve: then the patient must lie down on his back, and you mark out with encaustic three cautery points according to this figure and the same quantity below the spleen near the hypochondria, where a man's elbow reaches: and let there be space between each cautery point according to the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery point be straight according to the length of the body: and do not press your hand with the cautery too much.
And let the quantity that is burned be according to the thickness of the skin, a quantity not exceeding half of it: and let the patient stand on his feet.
But if he cannot stand, then let him lie down, extending his legs and raising his arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And it is possible for you to cauterize these points with a knife cautery when you have subtlety and skill in the art.
And be careful not to proceed too deeply in cauterization, so that the entire thickness of the skin is not burned, causing the whole body to be burned and reaching the intestines: for the skin there is thin, so you should know this.
On the method of cauterizing abscesses of the liver.
When it happens that one is about to die, and you wish to know if that swelling is in the flesh of the liver or in its covering: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, the sick person suffers pain and heaviness without sharpness; and if it is in the covering of the liver, there is with the pain a very intense sharpness; and you see now that its treatment has fatigued its doctors.
Therefore, the sick person should lie down on their neck. Then mark the location of the abscess with encaustic: then heat the cautery which resembles a rod. And this is its form. And cauterize with it once, until the skin is completely burned and reaches the siphac, until all the pus comes out: then treat it with the treatment for burns, until it heals.
And one should not use this type of cautery unless their study in the art of medicine is prolonged: and through whose hands such illnesses occur repeatedly with experience: then indeed they may dare to perform such an operation.
But to leave it alone is better in my opinion.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in pleurisy.
The ancients said, the cautery with roots of aristolochia for cold pleurisy according to this method. And it is that you take from the dried long roots of aristolochia one longer root, which is found among them, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then dip it in oil: and light it on fire. Then cauterize with one cautery where the fork joins the neck, and with two small cauteries below the slightly sloping area towards the part under the beard.
And with two cauteries also where the fifth and sixth ribs slope towards the back slightly: and with another cautery on the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from the back: one where the two spatulas meet: and with two cauteries from the two sides of the chest, the lower cautery being between the two spatulas.
And you should not compress your hand with the cautery, but let the skin be clearly smelled.
And some ancient ones have said that there are men who use a cautery similar to a rod: and they heat it, and insert it between the ribs until they reach the abscess with it, and the pus comes out: as we have said about the abscess of the spleen.
But in this puncture with the cautery, there is a fear that either the patient dies immediately, or an ulcer forms at the site, which has no cure.
Regarding the Method of Cauterizing the Spleen Chapter XXXII.
When you treat the disease of the spleen, and your treatment according to what we have said in the section on the treatment of diseases does not help, then cautery is applied in three ways, all of which are correct.
One is to make three cauterizations or four by lining according to the length of the spleen according to the figure of the cauterizations of the liver, whose figure preceded.
And there should be between each cauterization the thickness of a finger, or more or less.
And the method of the cauterization, which we have mentioned for the cauterization of the liver, should be equal.
And do not compress your hand with the cautery: and let the patient lie supine on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: to ignite a cautery having two prongs, which we have mentioned in the chapter on the dislocation of the shoulder: and elevate the skin which is directly over the spleen, where the patient's left elbow reaches: and your elevation should raise the skin according to the width of the body, so that the cauterizations fall according to the length of the body.
Then insert the two prongs that are very hot until you penetrate the skin from the other side: then withdraw the cautery: thus four cauterizations are made.
And if you wish, cauterize with another cautery having three prongs.
Then care for the cautery after you leave it to discharge pus over many days: for it is more beneficial than all that have preceded in the treatment.
Regarding the method of cauterization in hydrops.
The cautery does not apply in hydrops unless properly positioned.
When you treat the water-retainer with the methods of treatment we have mentioned in the division, and if the treatment does not help, then you must cauterize him with four cauteries around the navel, and one caustic on the stomach, and another caustic on the spleen, and two cauteries behind the back between the vertebrae, and one directly on the chest, and another directly on the stomach: and the depth of the caustic should be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cauterization open so that it discharges pus over a long period of time.
And do not evacuate the weak from treatment after cauterization with it; two intentions should be gathered for him: and healing will hasten to him with God's help.
The form of the caustic with which the stomach is cauterized should be key-shaped, according to its previous form; and that with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped, according to its previous form.
Regarding the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When abscesses form in the water-retainer and are filled with yellow water, you must cauterize on the back of the foot at the nocker, which is between the toe bone and the ankle: lift your hand with the caustic and do not twist it; then lift your hand: and do not repeat it at all.
For yellow water will sweat out, and the caustic should be in this form.
Then make two cauteries on both legs, on every leg, and let the cautery be made with the edge of the knife-like cauterizing tool: and let one cautery be made according to the length of the leg, one below the knee, and another below it, about the middle of the leg: and on each hip two cauteries: and leave the open cautery without treatment for a long time: so that some water may sweat out from it: then treat it with the other things we have said.
On the method of cauterizing for the treatment of abdominal conditions.
Chapter Thirty-Five.
When the abdominal condition arises from cold and humidities, until it weakens the retentive and digestive powers which are in the stomach and intestines: and it is treated with methods of treatment, and does not heal: and you see the patient tolerating the cautery of excessive power, then cauterize him with a large cautery on his stomach, according to what preceded in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery, and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a subtle key-shaped cautery: and a large cautery on the alcatin above the alhosos, or two cauteries.
And if you see excessive humidities and the patient tolerating it, then cauterize him with a cautery on the comb area, and a cautery on all the ilium: and perhaps you may add two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one.
For it is an effective treatment whose benefit does not fail.
On the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the year, or one, and they are from thick, cold humors, or corrupted moisture, and they are treated with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help: then cauterize three times above the lower spine under almeidati momentarily in a triangular shape, and below the navel with a cautery almost two fingers wide.
And if you think that his stomach is overly cooled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face becoming swollen with pus, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cautery as previously described: and with a cautery on his liver, and another on his spleen with a key-shaped cautery: and leave the cautery open for some time: then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you cut off althelul, then heat the cautery which resembles a rod. Then insert the heated cautery into the cut althelul: and hold it until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which the blood flows: do this once or twice.
If there are many althelul, then cauterize each one with a cautery as we have described. Then treat them with what heals them from ointments until they are healed.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery over linen, it is more ultimate in healing.
On the method of cauterizing an anal fistula.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
When the patient does not obey the cutting and procedure which we have described in its proper place, and is frightened by it, perhaps he may be healed with a cautery.
When therefore an anal fistula occurs in someone and becomes old, pus runs from it, and corrupted humors. It is therefore more proper to probe it with a fine探针. Then know the quantity of its depth with a probe.
Then heat the cautery, which is like a rod. Then insert the heated cautery into the fistula itself and the length to which the claw entered.
And repeat the cautery on it until all the corrupted bodies are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the amount of your need.
And guard yourself from burning the nerve, if it is there, or large veins: or if the fistula leads to the bladder wall, or to the intestinal wall, then guard yourself from all these areas.
And do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy area: and you think that it is not penetrating.
Then care for the area until it heals.
If the area is sealed and materials are separated from it and remains so for a long time: then you know that it is now fully healed.
And if materials do not separate from it, then you know that it is penetrating, or there is a corrupted bone in its depth, or something like that, of which the recollection will come in its place.
Regarding the method of cauterizing the kidneys.
When pain occurs in the kidneys due to cold or severe wind, and it is reduced because of the patient's weakness, then it is necessary to cauterize it over almethen on the kidneys, with a claw-shaped cautery over the entire kidney, as previously mentioned.
And perhaps we cauterize it a second time on the almeidatum. Therefore, three lined ones will come. Therefore, they will be more last in healing.
On the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening occur in the bladder due to cold and moisture until the patient cannot retain urine, then cauterize it on the lower part of the sumen above the bladder, where the pubic hairs begin, and with one cautery on the right side of the sumen, and another on the left side of it: and let the length of that lateral cauterization be according to the size of a thumb knot: and cauterize it with the lower back cautery, or with two cauters if needed: and let it be according to what precedes the clavicle cautery.
On the method of cauterizing the womb.
When cold and moisture occur in the womb, preventing conception and corrupting its menses, and delaying their onset, and pain occurs at their arrival, then it is necessary to cauterize it with three cauteries around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with one cautery above alcatim below the back, or with two cauteries: and let the cautery be clavile.
On the method of cauterizing the ankle in dislocation.
When mucous humidities flow to the hip socket of Anchae, and become the cause of its departure from its place: and the sign of this is that one leg is extended over the other when they are placed together; and the site of dislocation is found empty in it.
Therefore, you must cauterize the affected area on the hip socket with a similar circular cautery: after you mark with ink around the socket, as it revolves: and let the socket itself fall in the middle of the circle.
If this cautery is not available to you, then cauterize it with three large olive oil cauterizations: and the depth of the cautery should be according to the thickness of the entire skin.
Then care for it until it heals.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in sciatica.
When pain occurs in the hip socket and its causes are cold and humidities: and the patient is treated with what we have mentioned in the division, but if the treatment does not help and the condition persists: then it is necessary to relieve the patient of thick humors with foul pills, or with artificial pills, and similars. Then cauterize him.
And the method of cautery in this case is according to two methods: either cautery with burning medicines, or cautery with fire.
The cautery with fire is according to many methods.
One of which is to cauterize above the lid of its container with three triangular cauteries, according to this form. And make their depth good or bad. And let the space which is between each cautery be the thickness of a finger: let the cautery be olive-shaped.
Sometimes, however, the cautery is made in the middle on top of the lid of its container. Therefore, there are four cauterizations.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form preceded in the cauterization of the dislocation of the lid, with one: so that the circle contains the entire lid.
And burn the thickness of the entire skin.
This is the method of the cautery for sciatica, when the pain is attached to the lid itself, and does not extend all the way to the hip and leg.
If it extends all the way to the hip and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries on the hip, on the spot where the patient indicates there is pain, and with your cautery on the caudal area four fingers towards the wilderness side: and let the cautery be knife-shaped.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin.
If the patient indicates that the pain extends nearly to the toes of the foot, then cauterize it where they indicate with a point cautery, three, or four, or more if it is needed.
And if he indicates that pain is under the knee towards the leg, then cauterize that place with one knife cautery.
And be careful in all your cauterizations so that you do not end up using the cautery to such an extent that you burn a nerve or a large artery, and thereby bring upon the patient severe harm or contraction.
And indeed I have seen one and another of those who cauterized above the ankle, and they ended up in cauterization, and the leg swelled until a tumor followed to the foot, and it was entirely perforated, and the entire foot corrupted; then came a rupture of the abdomen, and death followed that.
If pain is in both parts at the same time, cauterize both according to this method.
And some wise men said regarding the cauterization of anchae, for which this is the method of cautery. Make a similar cautery from iron, whose diameter is half a palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a kernel of a fingernail, or slightly less: and within that cautery be a third cautery.
And let the space between each cautery be the width of a thumb knot: and let the cauterizations be open on both sides: and their depth should be about one or two thumb knots: and make handles from iron suitably fitted to the cauteries.
Then it is heated in fire until it turns red and throws out sparks: then it is placed on the armpit of the sick person lying on their healthy side. Therefore, cauterize him with three round cautery devices in one turn.
Then leave him for three days. Afterwards, apply plasters with butter: and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat him with an ointment until he is healed.
Albucasis says, we have used this kind of cautery little, O sons, because of the terror of its appearance: and furthermore, because we find few who can withstand it.
However, it is one of the good cauteries for those who endure, and find its proper place.
The cautery with burning medicines is such that you make two jars having a perforated ring, through which descends the hinge of its lid made of brass or iron, the length of the wall: each should have two knots, or something like them, in their height.
And let the space between the two be the thickness of a finger, and let them be open both below and above: and let them be joined together tightly according to this form.
Then place it on the lid of the anchor, with the patient lying on their sound side. And press your hand strongly on the lid of the anchor. Then pour between the two circles with hot water, which has been heated briefly over fire, and keep it for the duration of an hour: and let the patient endure its biting sensation and burning, for he will find the biting like fire until the burning subsides.
Then lift your hand with the instrument, and clean the entire wound with warm water and sweet water; then leave it for three days.
And put butter on it until the blackness of the burn is removed: and leave it for several days, and pus will flow from it. For it is the last in healing.
Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
If the pain extends to the thigh or leg: make a poultice on that which contains water, according to what you did for the wound equally.
And this is the method of warm water: and I have already written about it in the treatise on the correction of medicines. Take alkali and unquenched lime, each one part: grind both, and place them in a new pot, whose lower part has one small hole according to the size that a finger can enter: and place under the bottom of the pot another earthen pot: and pour over the alkali and lime sweet water enough to submerge both by a finger's depth: after which you compress them with your hand firmly: and leave the pot until the sharp water descends to the lower part of the earthen pot.
Then gather all that water and pour it over another lime: and distill it until it is renewed.
For it will then be very strong in sharpness, which is used in many medical procedures and in cauterizing other parts of the body. For it makes the action of its fire.
And among the medicines are those with which the ankh is cauterized, even like tesiie, and cashew apple honey, and lime with soap, so that each is thoroughly mixed.
And Galen narrated the treatment of an ancient man's cure, by which he was cured of the pain of the ankh and the sciatic vein: and he praised it greatly. And he said that he did not need another treatment, and that he was cured with one attempt, until he reported that he perhaps entered a bath carried in, and exited it already healed.
And it is to be taken from green seitaragi: and if green is not found, take the dry, fresh: and grind it much with some fat, and place it on the ankh where there is pain, or leg, or in the thigh: and bind it, and leave it for a duration of three hours, or for a length that the patient feels the sedation of the burning. Then introduce him to the bath.
Therefore, when his body becomes moist, introduce him into the seat. For the pain retreats, and it is healed.
And you should know that one should not use a cautery with these medicines unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides said that goat dung, when it is used to cauterize the sciatic vein, helps it: and the cautery is made in this way. Take wool, and soak it in old oil, and place it on the deep spot that is between the big toe of the foot and the instep, and it is closer to the instep.
Then take dried goat dung, and ignite it in fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished. Then do it again. Do not cease to do this until the sensation reaches the nail through the intermediary and the pain ceases.
And this method of cautery is called Vaccinum cautery.
On the cauterization of back pain.
It sometimes happens that pain occurs in the back for many reasons, either from a fall, or from a blow, or from excessive evacuation, and similar causes, due to the infusion of cold and humid matter; and indeed cautery is only applicable in this particular type which arises from the infusion of cold matter.
Therefore, after evacuating the patient with foul pills and similar remedies, three lines should be made on the back where the pain is, according to the width of the affected area itself. Once you mark with encaustro five cauteries on each line, or more according to the quantity that comes from the patient's tolerance and strength: and the cauterization should be done with a cautery point.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries using a middle-claw cautery according to this form.
On the method of cauterizing at the beginning of hump formation.
This disease often occurs in small children.
And the sign of the beginning of this condition in children is: that it occurs upon him a tightness in breathing during elevation and movement: and you find at the last vertebrae of the spine and its joints, that it has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
Therefore, when you see it and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery according to this form.
And let the cautery take effect on every part of the vertebra equally: and if you wish, cauterize around the vertebra with a point cautery in two lines, or three: and let the points be close to each other.
Then care for the area until it heals with what we have said.
And beware, do not apply the cautery to the hump that occurs due to nerve spasm.
On the method of cauterizing in gout and joint pains.
When joint pains are caused by cold humidities that are poured out to any part of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is customary among physicians to call this gout properly.
Therefore, when gout caused by cold is treated with methods of cure and the pains are not removed, then the cautery removes them.
And it is so that you cauterize him after evacuation around the joint of the feet, with many cautery applications: and let the cautery be Oleum.
And if you need to prick on the surface of the foot, then do it with a puncture cautery. If the pains ascend up to the knees or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize over the entire knee with three or four cautery applications from all sides, with this same Clavus cautery.
If you need more applications of this cautery, then cauterize it. And do not plunge your hand with the cautery, but let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
If the pains ascend to the knees and the back, then apply what we have said about the cautery in its chapter.
If the pains are only in the hands, then prick around the joints as if two lines are drawn.
If the pains remain in the digits, then prick them on every knot and on the palm of the hand.
If the pains ascend after days to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both from all sides.
And do not evacuate the patient from good regimen or from the reception of medicines. For if good regimen is established and the phlegm is evacuated, he will be healed with the help of God by this cautery.
On the method of cauterizing in ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the intestine or hernia descends near the testicle: then you must advise the patient to abstain from food on his day. And let him use mild remedies so that the stool may descend from his abdomen.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back: and advise him to hold his breath until the hernia or intestine appears.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark with cautery below the rupture on the rim of the pubic bone, with a mark whose end resembles half a circle directed towards the upper part of the body.
Then apply the cautery with this form of fire until it turns white and sparks. Then reduce the intestine or hernia to its concavity. Then let the assistant place his hand on the area to prevent the intestine from protruding: and you have already parted the patient's thighs, and placed a cushion underneath him, and another servant is above his legs, and another on his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery on the mark, with your hand holding the cautery straight. And hold it until you reach the bone with it: or repeat with it another time, if you have not reached the bone with it on the first try.
And prudently observe from the exit of the intestine during your cautery hour, lest you burn it, and thereby cause either death or great harm to the patient.
And you should know that when you do not reach the mouth with the cautery, your operation does not help.
And it is necessary that the cautery for infants be fine, according to their size.
Then treat with other ointments until it heals.
And let the patient lie on their back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary that you provide nourishment for the duration of his healing, which soothes his stomach: so that the intestine does not come out during effort and defecation.
Then when he wants to rise after forty days, administer a properly made bandage, and let it stay for another forty days.
And he should be reduced in labor, and fullness of food and drink, and loud voices.
For when he follows this regimen, he is healed with complete healing.
And I will speak of the treatment of ruptures with incision in its chapter.
When ruptures occur in the rest of the abdomen and are initial, and you want to prevent them from worsening, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let one-third of it be burned from then on. Then care for it with what we have said: and nothing shall be added.
And some have said first: that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
After it is marked with encaustic, and a line is placed across the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line below. And place your hand in the middle with a key-shaped cautery.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Regarding the method of cauterizing for pains due to falls or blows.
Chapter XLVIII.
When pain occurs in some limbs due to a fall or blow, and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize with a Point cautery.
And the cautery should be suited to the entire member according to its size, and its sensitivity, and its weakness, and its strength, and the location of the twist, and the pain from it.
If it is healed by the first cautery, it is well. If not: then repeat on the same cautery.
For it is the custom of these pains to shift from one member to the adjacent one. Therefore, it is necessary to address them with cautery until the patient is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in leprosy.
Lepers are sometimes greatly helped by the cautery. And especially the type of leprosy that occurs due to the putrefaction of phlegm and melanchole: when you wish to cauterize it, consider.
If the leprosy is spreading, and you have treated it with what we mentioned in the division, and it does not subside nor remain stable: and you fear that the corruption may spread over the entire constitution of the patient: then cauterize him on the head with five cautery points: one in the middle of the known part of the head, and the second below it towards the forehead at the end of the hairline, and two on the two temples, and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And lastly, apply your hand with the cautery for a moment until it makes a small imprint on the mouth, and the scabs fall off: so that the expiration of gross vapors from it may be alleviated, and cauterize the spleen itself with the cautery as previously described.
If the leprosy has already spread over the patient and is clearly apparent: then it is necessary to cauterize with these cautery points which we mentioned in the chapter, and a cautery on the tip of the nose, and two cauteries on both jaws, and two cauteries on the cervical vertebrae, and six on the dorsal vertebrae, and one large one on the alahosos near the tailbone and one above it, on the almeidati: and two on the hips: that is, one on each hip, and two on the knees: one on each knee, and two on the shoulders, and two on the elbows, and two on the soft parts of his chest: and cauterize him on every joint, from the joints of his fingers and toes: and cauterize on every heel of his feet and palms of his hands.
And beware of the nerves which are above the posterior part of the heel, lest you burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with one cautery on the mouth of the pelvis, and another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the spleen.
And you should know that the more you apply the cautery, the greater the benefit and the more it helps.
And you should know that the sick person does not find pain in the cautery as much as healthy people do: because their body is already numbed.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be of size and smallness according to the members and joints: according to which precedes from the kinds of instruments.
Then care for the cautery with flour of the herb and honey, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in stupor.
When some member is numb, and it is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it does not heal, then cauterize the numbed member with cauteries according to the size or smallness of the member as it deserves.
And let your cautery penetrate slightly into the thickness of the skin. Then care for it with an ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes it is cauterized for a kind of numbness that affects the hand and foot, at the vertebrae of the back near the exit of the nerves that move that member: and the numbness is removed.
But let not one who is not wise in the anatomy of the members and the exit of the moving nerves presume upon it.
Chapter Fifty-One.
When Alvarus becomes old and none of the medical skills are effective in it: then cauterize over it with a deep cautery for a moment, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color changes.
Then treat it with flour of the herb, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and blood of dove, and blood of swallow: let there be one part of each; mix all these, and apply them on cloth, and keep in place until it heals.
On the method of cautery in cancer.
When cancer is beginning and you wish to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, as it surrounds.
The wise have said that it should be cauterized with the final cautery in the middle.
To me, however, it does not seem right: for I fear that it may ulcerate: and I have already seen this several times.
And it is better that it be cauterized around it with a circle, as we have said: or with many cauteries.
On the method of cautery in adubelati.
When someone has an abscess and its maturation is delayed either due to excess causing it or due to the age of the patient if they are frail and of little blood, or due to time, and there is a need to hasten the maturation of the abscess, then cauterize around it with many small cautery points. Then release her. For it will hasten with the maturation.
If you wish to pierce it with a cautery, then take this cautery, which has this form.
And place it in the middle of the abscess until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be applied so that the following patient may be relieved of the course of pus.
Then care for it until it is healed.
About the method of cauterizing in a corrosive disease.
Chapter LIV.
A corrosive is nothing but corruption in a limb that spreads and corrodes it: just as fire eats dry wood.
If you see a corrosive in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then use many cauteries, small and large clavi, according to what is suitable for the place where the corrosive is.
Then cauterize it from all sides until you root out the entire corruption and nothing of it remains entirely.
Then leave it for three days, and place ground sulfur with oil on the cauterized areas until all the eschars are removed, and all corruption is gone.
Then treat it with flesh-generating ointments.
If you see that after three days flesh is born with a healthy growth, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not, then apply the cautery again on what remains of the corrupted areas.
And it is treated with sharp medicine when it corrodes. For it rises up from the place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is faster for healing: and I have already mentioned its cautery with sharp medicine in the division: therefore take it there when you need it.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in claws and warts.
Chapter LV.
This illness often occurs in the lower parts of the feet: and it is a thick, filtered substance that harms the foot.
And there are two methods of cautery for these: cautery with fire and cautery with hot water.
As for cautery with fire, make a concave cautery instrument similar to an eagle's feather: it should be made of iron according to the size that can contain the claw on all sides: and let it have fine edges.
Then place it ignited upon the nail. Then revolve the hand with the cautery around the nail until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail: and leave it for three days until it begins to emit pus. Then apply plasters with wild apples, crushed with salt: and leave the plaster on it during the night. For it will be uprooted from its roots.
Then treat the area with a flesh-generating ointment until it heals.
If they are not converted and often occur on the surface of the body, especially in hands and feet: then apply a cautery with warm water: and it is as follows, take a tube made of metal, or iron, or from an eagle's quill: and place it over the nail, or splinter. Then pour a small amount of warm water into the tube: hold your hand, and revolve it with the pressure of your hand for a moment, so that the edge of the tube is imprinted on the root of the nail, and let the warm water find its way to the depth, to the root of the nail: and let the patient wait for a while over the effect of the warm water for one hour.
Then leave it, for the nail is uprooted with its roots.
Do this one by one until you have addressed all of them that are in the body.
Then treat them after they are uprooted with what generates flesh from ointments.
On the method of cautery in tremor.
When tremor occurs in someone due to cold in the nerve, or from quartan fever, or another cause: then it is necessary to cauterize him with four or five cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and a cautery between each vertebra, and a cautery on his chest, and a cautery on his stomach.
For tremor is calmed with olive oil cautery, and recovery from cold illness is hastened.
On the method of cautery for Albathir.
Chapter LVII.
Sometimes in the body, Albathir causes ugly eruptions, that is, pustules which are caused by corrupted thick materials.
Therefore, when they first appear, they should be cauterized on the entire head of the pustule with a fine cautery using myrtle wood, the end of which is ignited with fire. Or with the root of long Aristolochia. Or with a lentil-shaped cautery.
And sometimes the ademenul is cauterized at the beginning of its expulsion in this manner: and they do not increase: and the excess causing them is dispersed, and they are healed from them.
However, it should be done after evacuation with bloodletting.
On the method of cauterizing in the flow of blood from an artery in a wound.
Often it happens that blood flows from an artery which is cut at a wound, whether occurring externally, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cauterization of a limb, and similar cases; and it becomes difficult to stop it.
