Then apply it to it repeatedly until it dries out.
And beware, do not perform this treatment at the beginning of the onset of the abscess. For it generally aggravates the abscess: and you should not do this unless the abscess is turning away from its hot state.
If this instrument is not available to you, then take a reed, and attach a piece of onion skin to its end so that the mouth of the sick person is not burned: because the onion skin prevents the vapor from burning the mouth: and this is a good treatment that ensures safety.
Regarding the removal of spines and bones from the throat.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
Often a bone adheres in the throat, or a spine of a fish, or something else.
Therefore, you must extract what is apparent from them upon which sight falls, after pressing the tongue with an instrument near the mouth, and it is made clear to you what is in the throat.
And what is not apparent to you and is hidden in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach. For perhaps the attached object will be expelled by vomiting.
Or let the patient swallow a piece of onion, or a root of lettuce, or swallow a piece of dry bread: or take a piece of soft dry sponge: and tie it to a string, then swallow it. When it reaches the place where the spines or bones are, and is pulled out, then it comes out.
If it does not come out with what we have said, then use an instrument made of lead according to this shape.
Let it be thicker than the radius slightly, and at its end let there be a curve, which can be inserted into his throat with ease: and he should hold his head raised up.
And let him be careful not to touch his epiglottis, so that he does not cause a cough, and push with it the bone, or spine, or let the physician insert it with his own hand.
But what the patient inserts is better: because of his knowledge of the location of the attached object: and push it downward, or pull his hand upward with the instrument, doing all this according to the amount prepared for him, until it comes out.
On the extraction of the leech.
Chapter XXXIX.
When the leech is treated with what I said in the division on treatment with medicines and it does not help, then examine the throat of the patient in the sunlight, or near the sun, after you press his tongue with the instrument that I described to you.
If therefore your sight falls upon the leech, extract it with a small hook, or with fine tweezers properly.
If it is not possible with them: then take a concave tube, and insert it into the throat of the patient near the throat; then insert a heated iron into the concavity of the tube. Do this many times: and let the patient abstain from water for the whole day.
Then let him take a vessel full of cold water, and open his mouth over it: and bring his mouth close to it without swallowing anything from it: and move the water with his hand every hour. For the leech immediately falls off when it feels the water.
If it does not come out with what we have mentioned, then fumigate the patient with bugs, or with ash with the instrument that I described for fumigating the uvula.
Do this many times, for it will fall off.
And the method of operation in fumigation is to take a pot in which there are burning coals with fire: and the pot should be covered with a cover, in the middle of which there is a hole: and the end of the instrument should be placed in that hole.
Then throw the fumigation, and let the sick person put his mouth at the end of the tube, and close his mouth so that the fumigation does not escape, until you know that the fumigation has now reached the leech. For the leech will fall immediately.
If it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times.
And let the sick person bear thirst, and eat salty food, and garlic, and not drink water.
Therefore, it is necessary to proceed with this regimen.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the leech is extracted from the throat when it falls into it by sight.
It is similar to forceps, as you see: except that it has this curvature which is inserted into the throat. And its end is similar to the mouth of a bird called the stork, in which there is the roughness of a file: when it grasps something, it does not release it at all.
Concerning the opening of abscesses, their incision, and general care.
Chapter XL.
There are many kinds of abscesses, of various forms, according to the recollection of them, namely, one and another in this book: and they are diverse in their puncturing and incision in two ways.
One of which is from the kind of abscess in itself, and that which it encompasses from humors.
And the second mode is due to places, in which it occurs in the body.
For an apostem occurring on the head is different from an apostem occurring on the anus: and an apostem occurring in a fleshy part is different from an apostem occurring in joints: and each of them has its own judgment based on the operation.
And among the apostems are those which should not be lanced until the pus in them is mature and complete: and among them are those which should be lanced while they are raw and do not mature according to completion.
Like the apostemata which are near the joints.
For when an apostem occurs near a joint and prolongs itself into it, until what is around it putrefies, the ligaments or nerves of that joint may be corrupted: hence it is a cause of the contraction of that member.
Or the apostem is near a principal member: for if you delay piercing it until it matures, it will harm either that member or the principal member through it.
Or it is near the anus, pierce it therefore while immature: and you should not pierce an apostem that is raw and not fully digested, unless it is near the anus, so that deep putrefaction does not occur and extend to the interior of the anus, and a fistula is formed, or something incurable results at its end.
You must know the time for piercing an apostem that has matured according to completion: and this is when there is a subsiding of pain, recession of fever, and reduction in redness, and pulsation, and sharpness at the head of the apostem: and other signs.
And it is necessary that you make the same perforation in the lower part of the abscess, and of greater prominence: and let the perforation extend along the length of the body, if the abscesses are in parts of hands and feet, and in regions of tendons, and cords, and nerves, and arteries, and finally in all equal places where there is no reflection.
In those that are reflected, proceed with the perforation according to that member.
When the abscess is in fleshy parts: then it is better to leave its perforation until its digestion is confirmed, as we have said according to the completion.
For if you pierce it before that, the course of the pus from it is prolonged, and there is much filth and foulness, and perhaps its lips and depth harden.
And some abscesses are pierced according to the width of the body in necessity: or according to what the member requires.
And it is necessary that you administer a small perforation in small abscesses, and a large perforation in large abscesses: or many incisions according to the similarity of the size of the abscess.
And there are abscesses in which it is necessary that the skin be scooped out: and cut when it has become like cloth, and reached the point where it is already dead: such as those that occur in many, like dules and buboes.
And there are some that are cut with a three-angled incision. And from them is one by which it is cut like the shape of a myrtle leaf.
As the groin abscess.
And from them are those in which round incision and lunar incision are administered: and similar to these from the incisions.
That which does not have a head, like mild superficial abscesses, should be pierced with a superficial puncture, or only flat.
And it is necessary, when the abscess is large, and has already collected much pus, and you pierce it, that you should not hurry and extract all the pus at that hour: rather extract a part of it. Then clean the abscess until the next day. Then extract some of the pus again.
Do this multiple times according to progression, until it stops: especially if the patient is weak in strength, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an elderly invalid: for the animal spirit is often exhausted from the body with the discharge of pus: and perhaps the patient dies, and you do not perceive it.
Therefore, be wary of this chapter with great caution.
And after your piercing with which you pierce these abscesses, it is necessary to clean the wound: and observe. If the wound of the abscess is small, or it is a flat incision, then apply lint from linen, or old cloth. And if there is a large abscess, and many perforating cracks are present, then you must insert linen into each crack until they meet.
And if you have cut away part of the skin in an abscess, or scraped around it: then you must fill it with old fat, or as when a cloth is stitched, or shaved with flax down without moisture: and bind it until the third day.
Then remove it and treat it with the appropriate ointment until it heals.
If a flow of blood occurs during your operation, then administer cold water and vinegar, after the cloth has been soaked in them: and place it on the site of the bleeding multiple times.
If the flow of blood persists, then you must administer treatment, and remedies, and powders, which I have described in many places in this book, and in divisions.
If it is during the winter season, and the site of the abscess is near many nerves: then you must pour powder with warm wine and oil over the areas: and place them on the sites.
And if it is during summer, and the areas are fleshy: then you must place powder soaked in water and oil, or with wine and oil, and all of that should be cold. Until the third day arrives, as we have said, then you must open the abscess, clean it, and administer appropriate treatment for its healing until it is healed.
This is therefore what is necessary from the knowledge of the treatment of abscesses universally.
According to the path of distinction, I have already spoken about every abscess, how the way to its cure is treated individually in chapters.
Chapter XLI.
On the incision of abscesses which occur on the scalp.
Small abscesses occur on the scalp, and they are of the species of Nodes, which are contained in the layers that serve as their sacs: they are like the fat of a hen.
And their kinds are many.
Some of them are fatty: some contain moisture similar to mud: some contain moisture similar to pus and boils: and others similar to these, and some are hard like stone.
And in the incision of all of them and their removal, there is no fear, as long as an artery does not contradict at their incision.
And the procedure for incising them is to examine them with an instrument whose form comes after this, which is called the Intromissum, until you know what it contains.
For if it contains moisture, then cut it with a longitudinal superficial incision: according to this form.
And begin the incision from line b to line g. When the moisture is evacuated, then remove the sac that contains the moisture, and do not leave anything of it entirely.
For it often returns if something of it remains.
Then submerge the bandage in Egyptian ointment, if it is present: and if not, in water and salt: and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day. For it will corrode what remains from the boil.
Then apply over the bandage with Egyptian ointment a second time, and a third, and if necessary do so until you are confident that nothing remains from the boil, then treat the wound with ointment until it heals.
If the aposteme contains a fatty knot: then cut it according to this shape, the incision having the form of a cross: and place hooks between the two lips of the incision, and scrape it from all sides: and endeavor with your skill in extracting the tissue that contains it.
If, however, the artery opposes you, then do what I will tell you next.
And similarly do for the aposteme, if it is stony, through cutting and treating it in the same manner as we have said.
And the incision on a stony aposteme is easier: because it contains little blood and moisture. And sometimes there are some of these apostemes that are on the head in certain individuals, which contain no moisture at all.
Which means: I cut into an aposteme on the head of an old woman, and found the aposteme like a solid, hard, rough, white stone that could not be broken: and if anyone were to strike it, it would wound them.
In other abscesses occurring in the head, apart from these abscesses which occur in the heads of children and near the roots of the ears, the incision of all of them should be superficial.
Or make the puncture from the lower part of them, so that the course of the pus may be directed downwards.
Then treat it with what is appropriate for its treatment.
About the incision of strophulas on the neck.
Chapter XLII.
These abscesses often occur in the neck, and under the jawbones, and in the groin: and sometimes they occur in the rest of the body.
And regarding those that occur in the neck, there can be one or many: and they are generated from each other: and every strophula among them is within its own proper coat, just as it is in the knots and abscesses of the head, as we have narrated.
And there are many kinds of these strophulas. And among them, some are stone-like: and some contain humors: and some are malignant, which do not obey treatment.
In that one which you see among them of good disposition to the touch, whose color is clearly near the color of the skin, and which moves in all directions, and is not attached to the nerves of the neck, nor to the glands, nor to the arteries, and is not deep: it is necessary to cut it with a superficial incision from the upper part to the lower part of the body along line b. to line g., and remove its skin from all sides: and extend the two lips of the skin with a hook, or with multiple hooks if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head, and extract it gradually.
And it is for caution, so that a vein or nerve is not cut.
And let the scalpel not be very sharp: so that it does not add to your hand with the incision, or disturb the patient, and you cut what is not necessary.
If however you cut a vein or artery and it prevents you from the operation, then place on the wound zegi powder, or certain powders which stop the bleeding, and bind the wound, and leave it until the sharpness of the inflammation subsides, and the wound softens: or it begins to turn and want to putrefy.
For the blood is stopped with a bandage. Return to your operation until you complete it.
Then probe with your index finger if any of the small Strophulus remain; then cut them and clean them.
If there is a large vein at the root of the Strophulus: then you must not cut that Strophulus from its root; rather you must tie it with a strong double thread, and leave it until it falls off by itself without harm.
Then fill the wound with old cataplasm that you have already submerged in Egyptian ointment. Then care for it.
If the entire Strophulus is cut, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound: and sew it immediately, as soon as you see that no excess remains.
If you see that excess remains due to the size of the Strophulus, then you must proceed to cut its root and remove it: and administer the suture as we have said.
And which contains moisture from the Strophuli, make a superficial puncture in it so that the site of its maturity may be apparent to you: and place the puncture below what follows next in the body, as we have said.
Then apply after the puncture a licinia with an ointment, and similar things to it, so that it corrodes what remains of the corruption, until when you see the wound already cleansed: then care for it with a flesh-generating ointment, until it is healed.
Chapter XLIII.
On the incision of the epiglottis caused by an abscess occurring in the throat.
The ancients said this incision in the epiglottis, and I have not seen anyone in our land who has done it: and this is the writing of their words.
In those who have synanche, it is necessary to avoid incision of the epiglottis: for no benefit is gained by it: because all the veins and lungs are weakened.
In those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or throat, or both tonsils, when there is no illness in the canal, it is necessary to use incision of the epiglottis, to avoid destruction which occurs from obstruction.
Therefore, when we want to do it, we should cut the epiglottis below three or four circles of the epiglottis, with a small incision in width, in what is between two circles by the amount that the section is in the soft part, not in the cartilage: and this location is suitable for incision because it is devoid of flesh, and blood vessels are distant from it.
If the surgeon is timid, then it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat with a hook. Then he should incise the skin until he reaches the canal: he should avoid the blood vessels, if he sees any of them.
Then he should cut the sifac which we mentioned: it is indicated upon the cutting of the canal by the phlegm that comes out of it, along with what is ruptured, and by the cutting off of the voice.
And leave the wound open for some time.
When the hour at which suffocation is feared has passed, bring together the two edges of the skin wound, and suture only the skin itself without the cartilage.
Then apply medicines that promote flesh growth until it heals.
Albucasis says. The summary of this discourse which we have narrated is not applicable unless they see that one of these abscesses has already burst in the throat of the sick person: and the patient is elevated above death, and wishes to cut off his breathing: they go to cut the Epiglottis so that the patient may breathe over the wound with some respiration and be saved from death: and for this reason they commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness is consumed, and it lasts for three days, or about that time: then they command to suture the wound and care for it until it heals.
And what I have seen with my own eyes is that one servant took a knife and thrust it into her throat, cutting a part of the windpipe.
And I was called for its treatment, and I found it to be roaring like the groan of a dead person.
I uncovered the wound, and I found the blood that had come out of the wound to be small. I was relieved that she had not cut the vein, nor the gut: and air was escaping from the wound.
I hurried and treated the wound, and cared for it until it was healed: and nothing happened to the servant except hoarseness of voice: and she returned after days to a better state of health.
Therefore, I say that there is no fear in the incision of the epiglottis.
Regarding the incision of the throat hernia.
Chapter XLIV.
This swelling named throat hernia is a large swelling according to the color of the body: and it is very common in women.
And it occurs in two ways: either it is natural, or it is accidental.
In the natural case, there is certainly no ingenuity.
The accidental, however, occurs in two ways: one of which is similar to fatty knots. And the other way is similar to the swelling that occurs from the knotting of an artery. And there is fear in it, and one should not presume to approach it with iron unless it is small: and you should examine it and investigate it with an introducer. If you find it similar to a fatty knot, and it is not hanging with any veins: then cut it like knots are cut: and extract it with what it contains from the cyst, if it is in a cyst: and if not, then examine all of it. Then care for the place with what is necessary for the healing, until it is healed.
Chapter Forty-Five.
On the cutting of various types of knots.
There are many types of knots, and I have already mentioned all their types in the division: and it is necessary that I describe here the difference between a knot and an excrescence: as it may cause confusion.
I say, therefore, that with an excrescence there is heat, and fever, and severe pains, until the effervescence of the excess subsides, and putrefaction is complete: for then the fever and heat subside.
With a knot, there is no heat, nor fever, nor pain, and they are contained in kistis sifachin, which is their own sac, and it is according to the color of the body: and their beginning is like a chickpea, and it becomes like a batecha, and may be larger or smaller.
And they are of two types: either fatty: or containing moisture. And the colors of the moisture are many, according to what I have said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the treatment of a knot, you should examine it and inquire about it first with an instrument called Intromissum, according to how its form will be presented in the chapter that follows this one.
And the method of investigation of abscesses and all nodules is to take this instrument and insert it into the wetter place which you find in the abscess: and you rotate your fingers with it gradually until you know that the instrument has penetrated the skin. Then move your hand according to the measurement of the size of the abscess.
Then withdraw what was inserted, and examine what comes out in its wake.
If then running moisture exits, whatever the color may be: then cut it with a superficial incision, as I have said in the case of other abscesses.
And if no moisture exits in the wake of what was inserted, then you know that it is dense: therefore cut over it with a cross-shaped incision, according to this form, as I have taught you: and suspend it with hooks, and remove the skin from all sides with ease: and keep the kistin on it if you can, to extract it along with the Node.
If, however, it is ruptured by blisters during the operation, and it is not possible to extract it whole, for this often happens, then extract it in pieces until nothing of it remains.
For if any part of it, whether small or large, remains, the Node will return in full measure.
If it overpowers you and a small part of it remains: then fill the wound at the end with some sharp corrosive powders: bind the wound, and place something warm over it where the abscess was: and care for it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
If therefore there is a large knot, then sew its two lips, and treat it with what causes flesh to grow.
If however there is a pulsating vein opposed to you, or non-pulsating: then hurry, and fill the place with ground zegi, and leave it tight for two days, or three, until the wound becomes putrefied, and the boiling of the blood ceases: then return to cutting what remains of the knot.
Chapter XLVI.
Regarding the instruments for cutting and piercing.
From these are the forms of introducers, and they are of three kinds.
From these is the large one, and from these is the medium one, and from these is the small one.
Let them be made of square-ended alfulud iron appropriately, so that they may facilitate entry into the abscess.
And these are the forms of the experiencers, and no, that is, the perforating ones: and one of them is named beris, that is, perforating: and they are of three kinds.
From these is the large one, and the medium one, and the small one.
They are used to investigate abscesses, exiturae, fistulas, and buboes from what is between them of bones.
And others are made round, smooth, and blunt, like large needles with which chairs are sewn, from citrus wood, or from brass, or iron, or silver.
And the better ones are those made from citron.
And there is also an experience with black lead, which is used to test fistulas, whose concavities have reflections, so that they are reflected with their softness with those reflections.
And there are again three kinds. For from them there are long ones, from them medium ones, and from them short ones, according to the amount of the width of the fistula and its constriction.
The form of hooks, and they are of many kinds.
For from them there are simple ones, that is, which have one curvature: and they are of three kinds as you see, Large, Medium, and Small.
And from them there are blind hooks: and they are of three kinds.
And from them there are hooks having two curvatures, and they are of three kinds: and from them there are hooks having three curvatures, and they are of three kinds: and all these are necessary in their place.
And these are the forms of scalpels, with which knots and abscesses are cut and skinned: and they are of three kinds: for from them there is a large, medium, and small one.
Their ends with which the cutting is done are sharp, other ends are not sharp: and they are not used in this manner, except to facilitate the skining of knots near the fear of cutting a vein or nerve: and so the patient may be healed and find temporary relief from the burning sensation found in the skining of abscesses.
They are made of metal and resemble a still with which alcohol is made: and at the wide end there are hidden points of spatula: and through it runs inward and outward as you wish, as you see.
The form of the spatulas which are hidden between the fingers for pricking abscesses: and the patients do not feel them: and they exist in three varieties, large, medium, and small.
The forms of air bladders with which the flow of blood is cut off: and they exist in three varieties, large, medium, and small.
They shall be made of metal or citrus wood, round, to a moderate length, as you see: and they shall be slender.
And it is necessary for you to have these varieties of air bladders, large and small, to cut off the blood quickly in an emergency, and then when medicine is not present for you.
However, do not use them to cut off blood in every part of the body, but only in fleshy areas: such as the calves of the legs, the hips, the arms, the nipples, the abdomen, the groin, and similar fleshy, moist areas.
And sometimes small instruments similar to the bark of pistachios are made from them, according to their shape: with which blood is cut off when it flows from the place of bloodletting or from a vein or artery incision: and sometimes they are made round in this form.
Chapter XLVII.
On the treatment of men's nipples which are similar to women's nipples.
Sometimes the nipples of some men swell at the completion of sleep (that is, when they begin to be polluted in sleep) until they resemble women's nipples: and they remain foully abscessed.
Therefore, whoever wishes to avoid this, should cut above the nipples in a crescent shape, according to this form from line b to line g. Then remove all the fat. Then fill the wound with a flesh-growing medicine. Then sew together the two lips of the wound, and care for it until it heals.
If the nipple inclines downward and softens because of its size, as happens with women: then it must be cut on both of its upper sides with two similar crescent-shaped cuts, each contained with the other at the ends of each, until there is a larger line containing a smaller one, according to this form from line b to line g. Then remove the skin that is between the two lips, and take away the fat, and administer what we have said about suturing and powders, which is necessary for the cure, until it heals.
If you cannot complete the incision that you need to make because of the patient's restlessness or due to blood flow: then you must fill the wound with a piece of felt dipped in a corrosive ointment, and leave it until it corrodes what remains of the fat. Then care for it until it heals.
On the piercing of an abscess, which occurs under the Titillico.
Chapter Forty-Eight.
These abscesses which occur under the Titillico, are of the species of hard Strophularium, which contains cysts, and from them come those that contain moisture.
Those that contain moisture must be cut with a crescent-shaped incision, according to this form, from line b to line g. When all the pus in the abscess has been evacuated, then fill it with old lint and leave it until the next day.
Then remove the lint and treat it with an appropriate ointment until it heals.
If the abscess is of the species of nodular Strophularium, then incise it as we have said in the incision over Strophulas equally.
If the wound extends to discharge pus, then apply a cautery to it as we have said in what has been mentioned before.
Chapter Forty-Nine.
On the incision of an abscess that occurs due to an Artery and Vein.
When an artery is ruptured and the skin above it becomes hardened, an abscess often results from this. And similarly, it happens to veins as well, causing an abscess and swelling in them.
And the signs by which it is known that the swelling and inflammation are due to the Artery and Vein are: for when the swelling is due to the artery, it is long, gathered in the depth of the body: and when you press the swelling with your fingers, you feel as if it were making a rustling sound.
And that which is due to the Vein, is round on the surface of the body.
And to cut upon this swelling is an error, especially when it is under the armpits, and in the groin, and in the neck, and in many parts of the body: and it is very large. Therefore, the care of it should be avoided with iron, and those that are even in the extremities or in the head should also be avoided.
Therefore, for that which of them is due to the inflammation of the arterial orifice, find a slit in the skin in length. Then open the slit with hooks, then the artery: and free it from the tunics until it is uncovered.
Then insert a needle under it, and make it penetrate all the way to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, according to which I taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples.
Then puncture the area between the two ligatures with a scalpel until all the blood within it is discharged and the swelling is resolved.
Then administer treatment that produces pus until the ligatures fall off: afterwards treat it with appropriate ointments until it heals.
If it is an abscess due to the cutting of a vein, then you must hold with your hand as much of the abscess with the skin as you can. Then insert the needle under the place you are holding with your hand, and make it penetrate: and let there be double thread in it until you draw it out from the other side. Then tie it with the abscess with a good ligature: according to what I told you about the ligature of the grape, from both sides with both ends of the thread.
If you fear that the thread will be pulled out, then insert another needle with another thread under the entire abscess at the site of the needle's incision: press and gather your threads at four places.
Then cut the abscess in its middle until what is inside comes out: then cut off the excess skin, and release what was tied from it.
Then place on it the poultice which you have submerged in wine and oil. Then administer the treatment which is done with plasters and ointments until it heals.
Chapter L.
Regarding the abscess that occurs from the twisting of nerves.
Just as an abscess occurs in arteries and veins, so too can an abscess occur in nerves: which happens due to a blow, or from excessive labor, and similar causes: and it most often occurs in the areas of the helpers, or heel, and in any place where joints are moved: and this abscess is severe.
Its color resembles the rest of the body, and it is in most conditions without pain: and when it is squeezed with vehemence, the patient feels a sensation like stupefaction.
And it is not a collection of pus gathered deep within the body, but rather it is beneath the skin, and it can be moved in all directions, and it does not move forward or to the front, nor backward to the rear.
Therefore, what is present at the joints should not be penetrated with iron. For perhaps contraction may occur.
In those cases where it is on the head or on the forehead, incise the skin with a scalpel. If it is a small collection of pus, then hold it with forceps, and cut it off from the root.
And if it is large, then suspend it with a hook, and scrape it: then remove it, and close the wound with stitches: and care for it until it heals.
Chapter Fifty-One.
Regarding the incision of an abscess that occurs in the abdomen.
Certain individuals frequently develop growths in their abdomens and other parts of their bodies, which are called Fungalia, by analogy to fungi.
Their root is subtle, and their head is large, and their lips are inverted. And some of them are small: and some of them become greatly enlarged.
And indeed I have seen a man, and in his stomach were two thelil, which were more like mushrooms than other things: there was no difference between them, white, small roots, and their lips were turned inside out, and they ended, and moisture always flowed from them.
So I cut them, and found one weighing almost ten and eight ounces and the other almost six ounces. The operation for cutting them is such that you should then consider if the patient is moist, and the color of the thelil is white, moist, fine roots: then cut it with a broad spatula, and have cauteriums ready in fire.
For often much blood is expelled at the cutting of it: therefore hurry if the blood overcomes you, then cauterize it.
If you see the patient fearful and timid about the cutting with iron, then take a properly made lead thread, and bind it to the athelul: whose size is as we have said, and leave it for two days.
Then add to the lead binding. Therefore, do not stop binding the lead whenever it impresses on the thelil, until it is severed and falls off by itself without effort.
If however the thelil has a thick root, then there is something to fear and be wary of in its cutting, especially if it is in the stomach.
However, it is possible to cut through the middle of it. Then cauterize it so that it does not return.
Then care for it until the wound heals.
And be careful not to presume to cut the tumor which is of a dark color, has little sensation, and an ugly appearance: for it is indeed a cancerous abscess: and I will come with a reminder of Cancer after this.
Chapter LII.
On the treatment of the navel prominence.
The navel prominence occurs for many reasons. Or from splits in the sifac, which is above the belly: and althub or intestine protrudes from it, according to what happens in other hernias. Or from the blood that flows from a vein or an artery, according to what has been mentioned. Or from wind confined in it.
If it is due to a split in the sifac and protrusion of thirbi: then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body: and it is soft, without pain: and its position varies. And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then its position is much more diverse than what we have mentioned. When you press it with your fingers, it is hidden: then it returns, and there may be a sound with it: and it swells greatly at the entrance of the bath, and causes great labor.
If it is due to moisture, then it is soft and does not disappear when you press it with your hand, nor does it shrink or increase.
If it is due to blood, then with these signs the abscess appears blackish from the swelling.
If it is due to flesh formed: then the abscess is heavy, thick, hard, and fixed according to a single quantity.
If it is due to flatulence, then its touch is gentle.
And the procedure in this case is to determine if the prominence of the navel is due to blood from arteries, veins, or flatulence: then you must refrain from treating it. For in this there is fear and dread, as I taught you in the chapter where I said about abscesses due to arteries and veins.
If the prominence of the navel is due to the intestine or hernia: then you must advise the patient to hold their breath and stand stretched out. Then mark with cautery around the entire navel. Then instruct him to lie down on his back between your hands. Then circle with a broad spatula around the navel on the area you marked with cautery. Then extend the middle of the abscess upward with a large hook. Then bind it firmly around with thread or with silk cord: and let the knot of the binding be strong.
Then open the extended middle of the abscess above the binding. If you find it already caught by the ligament: then extract the hernia, and insert your index finger into it, and push the intestine into the abdomen: and if you find a cicatrix, then take hold of it with a hook, and cut off its excess.
If, however, the artery or vein is opposite you: then tie it tightly around. Then return to your operation. And take two needles, and insert two strong threads into them: and insert the two needles into the circle you made around the abscess in the shape of a cross, which you make to penetrate.
Then grip the abscess at four places above the needles: and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave the area until the extended flesh putrefies: and it falls off by itself: or cut it when it thins out and putrefies.
Then treat it with the appropriate ointment until it heals.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to hardened flesh in it or moisture: then it is necessary to hollow out the abscess as we have said. And extract the blood or moisture that you find in it.
Then treat it with what strengthens the area.
Chapter LIII.
Regarding the treatment of CANCER.
We have already spoken about the classification of types of cancer and how to treat it with medicines: and we must be cautious when treating it with surgery so that it does not ulcerate: and we have discussed cancer generated in the uterus and precautions for its treatment.
And the ancients said that sometimes cancer is in a place where its removal is possible: such as cancer which is in the breasts, or in the thigh, and those similar, from members located for extracting all of it: especially when it is a small beginning.
When however it becomes old, and is large, you should not approach it.
For I was not able to heal anyone from it: nor did I see anyone before me who reached that.
And the operation on it, when it is located as we have said, is to proceed and release the patient from black bile several times. Then bleed it if you find it with obvious fullness.
Then prepare the patient for the preparation in which he is placed with the operation.
Then throw into the cancer hooks that are suitable for it. Then scoop it from all sides with the skin, according to examination, until nothing remains of its roots: and let the blood flow, and do not cut it quickly, but press the areas, and wipe off all the thick blood with your hand, or with whatever is possible there from instruments.
If, however, the flow of thick blood from the incision of an artery or vein opposes you, then cauterize the vein until the blood is stopped. Then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
Regarding the treatment of dropsy.
Chapter XLIV. We have already discussed in the division of the types of Hydropsis, and how the aggregation of water occurs: and the signs of every type, and its cure with medicines.
And that which is treated with iron is only the asclitis type alone: and it is not approached with iron in the timpanitis type: nor thoroughly in the hyposarcae type: for that is deadly.
When you have already treated this type of Hydropsis timpanitis with medicines, and your treatment has not helped: then consider. For if the weakness has already overcome the patient, or there is another illness with him besides Hydropsis: such as if he has a cough, or diarrhea, and similar conditions: then beware of treating him with iron: for there is fear in that.
But if you see a patient of abundant strength, and there is no illness with him besides Hydropsis alone: and he is neither a child nor an elderly person: then the method of treatment for him is that you lift the patient standing between your hands, and a helper behind him should press his belly with his hand to drive the water down to the lower part of the chest.
Then take a sharp instrument with spikes according to this shape. It should have two sharp points, long, with sharp ends like a spatula. However, it should have a gradual narrowing so that you do not penetrate through to the intestine with it during the procedure and injure it.
Then consider. For if the generation of hydropisis is from the intestines, then it is necessary to extend with a cut from the navel by the length of three fingers, downwards directly over the pecten.
But if the generation of hydropisis is due to disease of the liver: then let your cut be to the left of the navel by three fingers.
And if its generation is due to the spleen, then the incision should be on the right side: and it is also not appropriate for the incision to be on the side on which the patient wishes to lie, so that the excess fluids do not flow to that weak spot.
Then pierce the entire skin with the instrument. Then insert into that incision, and lift your hand with the spatula between the skin and sifac, as if you are removing the outer layer: and the amount to be removed should be the size of a fingernail, or around that.
Then pierce the sifac until the spatula reaches the empty space: and that is the location of the water. Then extract it, and insert into the opening an instrument, which has this form. And it is similar to a cannula: made of silver, or brass, or bronze, smooth, polished: at its lower part there is a small opening, and on its sides there are three openings, two from one side, and one from the other side: and the edge is the cut end according to the manner of cutting a reed, as you see: at its upper end there is a ring.
For when the instrument reaches the water, then it descends immediately on the instrument, therefore evacuate from water in an hour a medium quantity.
For if you evacuate more than is necessary from it, perhaps the sick person will die within an hour by the resolution of his animal spirit: or he may suffer a syncope that approaches death.
But evacuate from it according to the quantity of its power, and according to how the dispositions of the sick person signify to you from the strength of his pulse, and from his good condition.
Then remove the instrument, and retain the water.
Which is because it is retained immediately due to the skin which holds the hole that is on the siphon: of which I have spoken, so that you may pierce it according to that method.
Then repeat the procedure the next day, if you see the sick person tolerate it: and also evacuate a small quantity from the water.
Do this for several days without fear, and guard yourself from error: until there is only a little water left.
If you are afraid for the sick person and leave much water remaining: then treat him with burial in warm sand, and much sweating in a bath and sun, and expectorate upon thirst: and treat him with drying medicines until he is healed: and cauterize over the stomach, spleen, and liver, after the extraction of water: as I have narrated in what precedes.
Regarding the care of infants who are born with their urinary passages not perforated.
Chapter LV.
When one of the infants exits the womb of his mother, and his urethra is not perforated, or there is a narrow opening, or it is not in its proper place.
Therefore, it is necessary to intervene with its perforation immediately upon birth with a very fine spatula, according to this form.
Then place a thin pin made of lead in the opening and tie it: and keep it there for three days, or four.
When he wants to release urine, it should be removed, and he may urinate. Then replace it.
And if you do not place the lead, it is possible that the urine which flows over the area may prevent it from closing.
He whose opening is narrow is treated with lead, as we have said, for many days, until it is enlarged.
Those in whom the opening is not in its proper place are injured. This is because, in those who are born, the opening is at the end of the penis: therefore, they cannot urinate forward until they lift the penis upward with their hand. Nor can he procreate because the sperm cannot reach the womb properly: and it is a very foul disease.
And the method of the operation is to have the patient lie on his back. Then extend the head of the rod with your left hand forcefully, and cut off the head of the rod from the priapi location, with a sharp point or a sharp spatula: as is the cutting of a reed, or as you root something, so that its middle comes like the head of the rod: and so that a hole falls in the middle as it should.
And be careful at your operation from blood flow. For it often happens. Therefore, apply to it something that stops the blood, and treat the wound until it heals.
Concerning the conditions that occur in the foreskin and head of the penis, and regarding corruption, blackening, and adherence.
Chapter LVI.
These conditions often occur in the penis, and they are protrusions of foul flesh.
And from it, some are malignant, and some are not malignant.
Therefore, the non-malignant one should be suspended with a fine hook and cut off until you clean it all. Then place on it a cloth soaked in Egyptian ointment. Then treat it after that with dyafinicon ointment until it heals.
If the condition is malignant and of a foul color, then it is necessary to apply cauterization after its incision and treatment.
If however Albather is on the foreskin of a captive, not circumcised, and there is part of Albather between the foreskin, and part of it outside: then you must remove Albather which is inside first, until when it solidifies, then care for it externally: because when you care for it at the same time, the foreskin does not heal but becomes worse.
And it also happens that in the testicles and foreskin there is blackening and corruption. Therefore, you must hollow out all that is already blackened, and what is about to be corrupted, or is already corrupted.
Then apply on it after that honey which is already mixed with the flour of pomegranate rind, and crushed sieve herbs.
Then care for it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
If however a blood flow occurs, then apply the cautery with a crescent-shaped cautery, according to this form.
For cautery is beneficial for two conditions simultaneously, namely for blood flow and a wound when it becomes corrupted.
If the head of the penis is corroded and destroyed entirely within an hour: then you must insert a lead tube into the urethra so that the patient may urinate over it.
In cases where the foreskin adheres to the head of the penis, and this adherence does not occur unless in one whose foreskin is healthy and does not require circumcision: and sometimes it occurs due to a wound or an abscess: therefore you must scrape it with a blunt spatula until the bond is loosened and the head of the penis is freed on all sides.
If it is difficult to distinguish them precisely, then it is necessary to remove some from the head of the rod, and from the foreskin. Which is because the foreskin, when it is thin, perhaps is pierced quickly due to its thinness.
Then separate the foreskin from the head of the rod with a fine linen cloth that is already moistened in cold water, so that they do not stick together again.
Then it should be treated with astringent wine until it is healed.
Chapter LVII.
On the cleansing of infants, and the treatment of errors that befall them.
Circumcision is not a solution of continuity like other wounds; however, since it is by our operation, by our will, and its use is properly for children, it is necessary that we mark in it a better operation and a lighter way leading to healing.
I say therefore that the ancients did not mention circumcision in any of their books because they do not use it in their laws, and it is only what we have acquired through experience.
Which is because I found the majority of artisans and phlebotomists to use cleansing by circumcision with a lancet and scissors; and they use cautery, binding with thread, and incision with a knife.
And indeed I have already tested all these methods and have not found a better one than cleansing with scissors and binding with thread.
For in the cleaning with the lancet, the skin often escapes. For the skin of the foreskin has two layers: therefore perhaps the upper skin is cut, and the lower layer remains: thus it is necessary to make another incision to cut the other, causing future pain. And with the cleaning which is done by alfecti, that is, awls, which tailors use, it does not cut the extremity of the male member: because it might enter its opening.
In cleaning with the hoof, the iron might slip and ruin your operation: and the skin of a boy is short by nature, and often they are born in such a way that they do not need cleaning: and I have already seen this.
However, the cleaning with scissors and binding with thread has proven to be a good experiment for me: because the scissors are proportional in making the incision: therefore, the sharpness that is on top is like the sharpness that is on the bottom. When you press your hand, the two sharp edges are aligned, and they cut according to a single operation at the same time: and a compression of similar shape is made, holding the skin of the rod from all sides, with which there is no error at all.
And the method of the operation is to make the boy understand, especially if he is one who comprehends quickly, that you do nothing but tie a thread on his rod only: and leave him until the next day.
Then make him rejoice and be glad in every way that is possible for you, according to what his understanding receives. Then make him stand between your prepared hands, and let him not be sitting: and hide the scissors in your sleeve, or under your foot, so that the boy sees them not at all, nor any of the instruments.
Then insert your hand to his rod, and blow on the skin, and pull it up until the head of the rod comes out. Then clean it from what filth accumulates in it.
Then bind the marked place with a double thread. Then bind below that briefly with a second bandage. Then hold with your index finger and thumb the place of the lower bandage firmly, and cut between the two bandages. Then lift the skin up quickly, and extract the head of the rod. Then let the blood flow gradually (for it is better) and put powder on top: and on top of the powder a cloth in which is spread the yolk of an egg boiled in rose water, mixed with good fresh rose oil: and leave it on until the next day: and care for it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
The form of the scissors for cleaning is this.
Let the two ends be blunt and sloping: so that the branch of the nail does not protrude: and let the length of the two sharp edges be equal to the length of the two handles.
The error falling in cleaning is: for perhaps the inner skin altogether or part of it escapes at the incision.
Therefore you must extend it with your fingernail at your hour before the swelling of the place: and cut it according to equality.
If you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then remove it with a hook, and cut it.
If three days have passed and what is under the nail remains swollen, having formed an abscess: then leave it until the abscess ripens and becomes warm, and remove the scab with ease, and cut it according to how it is prepared for you: and beware of the tip of the nail. For it will not harm it.
Treat it with what strengthens the wound from the powders we have mentioned in the chapter on powders: and if it is cut beyond measure through the skin and extends to deeper areas, it will not harm it either.
Treat it with what we have said until it heals.
Chapter LVIII.
Regarding the extraction of retained urine in the bladder.
Retention of urine in the bladder occurs due to obstructions caused by stones, clotted blood, pus, or flesh growths, and similar things from those we have mentioned in the methods of treatment in the division.
And if the urine does not resolve and you see that its retention is due to a stone already in the neck of the bladder: then it is necessary for the patient to be bent over on his knees. Then let his feet be placed upon his back, and let his belly be extended from the upper part of his back, and let the patient hold his breath as much as possible. Therefore, it is drawn with the neck of the bladder for the expulsion of the stone to the back: hence the urine is discharged.
If it does not resolve with what we have said and the condition is severely affecting the patient: then you must administer its extraction with an instrument called a syringe, which has this form: It should be made of silver, and be delicate, soft, hollow like the quill of a bird's feather in thinness, long like the length of one and a half palms; it should have a fine tube at its head.
And the method of urine exiting through it is to take a doubled thread, and tie wool or cotton at its end with a good knot: and insert the end of the thread into the lower part of the syringe: and cut with scissors if there is any excess wool, but insert it into the tube forcefully, like an awl.
Then anoint the syringe with oil or butter, and egg white: and have the patient sit on a seat, and pierce the bladder, and his rod with moist oils, and olive oil, and warm water.
Then insert the syringe into the rod easily until it reaches the root of the rod.
Then double it above the navel.
Then push the syringe inside until it reaches the bladder, and let the patient feel that it has reached the empty space: and this is not done according to this order unless because the passage through which it goes is twisted.
Then extend the thread with wool gradually. For Vrina will follow the wool.
Then withdraw it, and make Vrina run through the urine passage: and repeat the syringe, and do not cease to do this until the bladder is emptied, and the patient finds relief.
Regarding the quality of cystoclysm with a clepsydra.
Chapter LIX.
When an ulcer occurs in the bladder, or blood congeals in it, or pus is confined in it, and you wish to distill into it waters and medicines: then it should be done with an instrument which is called a clepsydra, and this is its form.
For it is closed, that is, sealed. And in it there are three holes, two on one side, and one on the other side, as you see.
And the concave area, in which is what pushes, should be according to the size that fits it without addition, until when something is drawn with it, moisture is attracted: and when it is pushed, it is expelled far away: as a clepsydra does, with which naphtha, that is, Greek fire, is projected in battles.
When you wish to project moisture into the bladder, insert the end of the clepsydra into the moisture, and draw with it what pushes upward, for the moisture is drawn into the concavity of the clepsydra.
Then insert its extremity into a rod, as we have narrated in the syringe. Then push the moisture with that which pushes it, for that moisture reaches the bladder immediately, so that the patient feels it.
The form of a subtle clyster with which the bladder is cleansed.
Let it be made of silver or brass, whose head should be higher and similar to a small alcamah, and below it there should be a groove in which the ligament falls.
Then take the bladder of a ram and put the moisture in it with which you wish to cleanse the bladder. Then tie it between two grooves with a strong ligature using double thread: and warm that moisture slightly over the fire.
Then insert the extremity of the clyster into the rod, then press your hand over the bladder with a proper tightness along with the moisture until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
If you do not have a bladder available, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it entirely around its circumference. Then insert a strong thread into those holes as they revolve. Then assemble the circle as you would assemble a container: after which you place in it what you wish from moisture, oils, and waters.
Then tie it to the instrument: and do with it as you did with the bladder by expressing it with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
Chapter LX.
On the extraction of the stone.
We have already discussed the classification of stone types and their treatment with medicines. I mentioned the difference between stones generated in the kidneys and bladder, and the signs of each. I also talked about the stone on which manual operation and incision are performed, which is properly generated in the bladder, and that which attaches to the penis. And I am narrating this with clear explanation and abbreviation.
I say therefore, that the stone generated in the bladder most often occurs in boys.
And among its signs is that urine exits the bladder similar to water in its fineness, and white sand appears in it, and the patient rubs his penis and labors with it, and hangs down frequently. Then it erects, and the anus protrudes with it in many of them.
And the healing of boys is easy up until they reach fourteen years of age. And it is difficult in the elderly. In young adults it is intermediate, between the two extremes: and for those whose stone is larger, the treatment is easier; and if smaller, the treatment is conversely more difficult.
Therefore, when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with a clyster that will expel all the feces in their intestines, for it sometimes prevents the discovery of the stone during the examination.
Then let the patient be taken with his feet and shaken, and moved downwards: so that the Stone may go down to the bottom of the bladder, or jump from a height several times.
Then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be under his hips, so that the bladder may be entirely inclined downwards.
Then examine him, and touch him from the outside.
If therefore you feel the Stone in the space, then immediately proceed with the incision over it.
If it does not fall under your touch at all, then you must clean the index finger with oil from the left hand if the patient is a boy: or the middle finger if he is a full-grown youth: and insert it into his anus, and examine for the Stone until it stands under your finger: and gradually turn it toward the neck of the bladder.
Then press on it with your finger, and push it outward toward the place where you wish to make the incision: and command one attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and command another attendant to raise the testicles upward with his right hand: and with the other hand, to move away the skin which is beneath the testicles from the area where the incision is made.
Then insert the cutting spatula, which has this form. And find the area between the anus and the testicles, not in the middle, but to the left side of the genitals: and make the incision over the stone, with your finger in the anus: and let the incision be transverse, so that the outer part of the incision is wider and the inner part narrower, according to the amount that the exit of the Stone from it should not be larger.
Perhaps indeed the finger compresses the stone within the anus at the incision, and it comes out without difficulty.
And you should know that from the stone which has angles and edges, its exit becomes difficult because of that.
And from it is smooth, similar to a gland, and round: and its exit becomes easy.
Therefore, for the one that has angles and edges, add to the incision.
If it does not come out thus, then you must be ingenious with it: either grasp it with forceps properly, the end of which is like a crescent, which grasps onto the stone and does not slip away: or insert under it a subtle instrument with a curved end.
If however you cannot grasp it, then enlarge the opening slightly. If anything from the blood overpowers you, cut it with a scalpel.
If however there is more than one stone, then first push the large one toward the mouth of the bladder. Then incise above it. Then push the small one after that: and do likewise if there are more than two.
If it is very large, then it is unskilled to cut it with a large incision. For it happens to the patient one of two things, either that he dies, or there is a continuous dripping of urine: because the place does not heal entirely.
But administer the expulsion of it until it comes out; or remove the pieces in its fracture with scissors until you extract it bit by bit.
When therefore you have completed your operation, then fill the wound with incense, and aloe, and dragon's blood: and bind it, and place over it a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or rose oil, and cold water: so that the warm pus may settle.
Then place the patient on their back, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day. When therefore you loosen it, moisten the area with water and much oil.
Then treat it with diaphyfortium ointment and basilicon ointment until it heals.
If, however, a warm pus and corrosion and similar things happen in the wound: such as if blood congeals in the bladder and urine is prevented by it: and this is known by the discharge of blood with urine. Therefore insert your finger into the wound and draw out that blood. For if it remains, it causes the corruption of the bladder and its putrefaction.
Then clean the wound with vinegar, water, and salt: and treat it with everything that is suitable for its healing until it is healed.
And it is necessary during the entire course of treatment to bind the two thighs together for the purpose of the medications that are placed on the area.
If the stone is small and is in the channel of the penis and is stuck there and blocks the passage of urine: then treat it as I describe before you come to incision. For often you will be spared from incision through this treatment, for I have already proven it.
And it is that you take the perforator from Afghan iron, whose form is this, with a triangular end, sharp, fixed in wood.
Then take a thread and tie the penis with it under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder.
Then insert the perforating iron into the penis with ease until the perforator reaches the stone itself: and rotate the perforator with your hand on the stone gradually: and try to penetrate it until you make it go through the other side.
For the urine is expelled immediately.
Then press your hand on what remains of the stone from the outer part of the penis. For it breaks apart and exits with the urine, and the patient is healed.
If this treatment is not prepared for you, because of something that prohibits it: then tie a thread under the stone and another thread above the stone. Then cut above the stone on the penis between the two threads. Then extract it. Then loosen the binding and clean the clotted blood that forms in the wound.
And it is not necessary to tie the thread under the stone except so that it does not return to the bladder: and another binding above, unless when the thread is loosened after the exit of the stone, the skin returns to its place and covers the wound: and for this reason you must do this when you bind the upper thread, so that you raise the skin upwards, so that it returns at the completion, and covers the wound, as we said.
Chapter LXI.
On the removal of stones in women.
A stone is rarely generated in women.
If, however, a stone should occur in any of them, then the treatment is difficult, and it is prohibited due to many reasons.
One of the reasons is that the woman may be a virgin.
And the second reason is that you do not find a woman who will expose herself to a doctor when she is chaste, or among those who have husbands.
The third reason is that you do not find a woman who is well knowledgeable in this art, especially the manual procedure.
And the fourth reason is the distance from the location of the stone: therefore, it requires deep incision, and there is fear in that.
If necessity provokes to do that, then you must take a woman doctor who is well knowledgeable: and she is rarely found.
If you are deprived of that, then seek a chaste and subtle doctor, and present a well-instructed midwife in women's matters, or a woman who has some knowledge in this art: therefore, make her present, and especially let her do everything you instruct regarding the inquiry about the stone.
First of all, he should check if the woman is a virgin: then he must insert his finger into her anus and search for a stone.
If he finds it, he should press it with his finger, and then instruct the midwife to insert her finger into the patient's vagina and search for the stone, after placing her left hand on the bladder and compressing it firmly.
If he finds the stone, then he must gradually move it from the bladder's opening downward with all his strength until he reaches the root of the hip with it.
Then he should incise above it at the midpoint of the vagina near the root of the hip, on whichever side he feels the stone: and his finger should not be removed from the stone, pressing under it; and let the incision be small at first. Then he should insert a probe above that incision.
Then he should insert a probe above that incision. If he feels the stone, then he should increase the incision according to the amount proportional to how the stone exits from it.
And you should know that there are many kinds of stones. Among these, there is a small one and a large one, smooth and rough, long, and round having branches.
Know therefore its kinds, so that it may be indicated to you by this concerning what you desire.
If blood overpowers you, then apply ground zego to the area and keep it for one hour until the bleeding stops.
Then return to your operation until the stone comes out: and do so that you prepare with you from the instruments which I said in the extraction of the stone in men, to assist you through them in your operation.
If the flow of blood overcomes you, and you know that the expulsion of blood is from an artery which has been cut: then put powder on the place, and bind it with bandages tightly: and do not change it: and leave the stone, and do not extract it. For perhaps the weak woman will die. Then care for the wound.
Therefore, when the sharpness of the blood is calmed after days, and the place becomes putrid, then return to your operation until the stone comes out.
Chapter LXII.
Regarding the incision of a watery hernia.
Watery ramex is not present unless there is an aggregation of moisture in the sifac alb, which is beneath the skin of the testicle containing the ovum: and it is called sifac.
And sometimes it is in its own pouch, which nature has prepared for it in the part of the ovum until it is ripened: which is another ovum, and it is the skin of the testicle between the sifac alb, which we mentioned: and that does not occur except rarely.
And the generation of this ramica is from the weakness that befalls the testicles: therefore this material is discharged to them. And sometimes it happens from a blow on the testicles.
And this moisture has many colors. For its color either tends towards yellowness, or is blood red, or feculent black, or is water white, and that which is more is like that.
And the signs by which it is known where the aggregation of water is, are these. For if there is in the white scrotum that we mentioned, then the abscess is round in length somewhat like the figure of an egg: and the testicle does not appear, because the moisture contains it on all sides.
And if the moisture is in its own little pouch, then the abscess is round like a part of an egg, and because of this, a person thinks that it is another egg.
And if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white scrotum, then it falls under sensation.
When therefore you wish to know the color of the moisture, then test the color of the moisture in the abscess with a square probe, whose form preceded. According to what emerges in the track of the probe, judge of that which is within it.
When therefore we come to the treatment with iron, then it is necessary to advise the patient to be bled if it is possible for him, and you see his body full.
Then he should lie on his back on something slightly elevated, and place many cloths under him.
Then sit you on his left, and command the servant to sit at his right, who extends the rod to one of the two sides of the scrotal skin, and to the pubic region of the abdomen.
Then take the broad scalpel and cut the scrotal skin lengthwise in the middle, almost to the pecten: and let the incision be made according to a straight equidistant line that divides the scrotal skin until it reaches the white sifac covering: and peel it off, and beware from this, so as not to cut it: and let your peeling be on the part that hangs more with the egg: and carefully examine with the peeling according to what is possible for you.
Then pierce the water-filled sifac with a wide puncture, and draw out all the water.
Then separate the two lips of the incision with hooks, and extend the sifac upwards, and do not touch the scrotal skin that covers it: and cut the sifac however it is possible for you to cut it, either in its entirety or piece by piece, especially the thin side of it. For if you do not examine it thoroughly, security is not achieved in its incision, lest the water return.
If the egg protrudes outside its skin during your operation, then when you have completed the incision of the sifac, reduce it back. Then bring together the two lips of the scrotal skin with sutures.
Then care for it like other wounds until it heals.
If you find an egg corrupted by other blackness, then it is necessary to tie the vessels which are the suspenders, fearing a flow of blood.
Then cut off the testicle with the suspender, and extract the egg: then treat it as we have said.
If water has gathered in two parts, then you know that there are two branches: therefore cut the other part equally as you did with the other.
And if it seems to you that the operation is one, then do as follows: afterwards clean the blood. And insert into the incisions wool soaked in oil, or in rose oil: and place outside another piece of wool which you have soaked in wine and oil, and spread it over both testicles, and around the belly: and place on top doubled cloths, and they are poultices: and bind them with a bandage that has six according to this form.
Then let two cloths be taken, and sweated, and filled with ground laudanum according to this pattern: and the ends by which it is pressed should be made of chamois or wet wool: and gathered together with a binding around the waistband of the breeches: and one end should cover from the anus up to the back, and the second should cover towards the hip area: and two ends above the two thighs below, and the other two ends over the two groins, and let the entire binding gather at the waistband of the breeches.
And sometimes this branch is treated artificially with a cautery instead of incision with an iron: and it is that you take a fine knife cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles with it: and it is ignited as we have described: until when the white membrane containing water is revealed: then take the cautery according to this form.
It is assimilated to the Greek letter.
Then pierce it with that heated iron until all the moisture comes out.
Then extend the scalpel with hooks, and remove the surface with a fine heated cautery, and cut it as much as you can until you root out all of it.
And be careful with the egg, lest the fire touch it.
And you should know that this operation is safer, farther from blood flow, and better than the operation with incision.
If however something opposes you at the time of incision, or at the time of cauterization, such as a warm aposteme, or blood flow, or anything else: then you must treat what opposes you with the cure that is appropriate to it, according to what has been stated.
If however the patient is timid and does not bear this operation due to its horror: then administer the piercing as I describe it, and it is done.
When it is confirmed to you by what we have said about the signs that the ramex is watery, then it is necessary to make the patient sit on an elevated seat.
Then pierce the aposteme on its lower part with a broad spatula: and make the piercing according to the length of the body, and let the opening be wide until all the water flows out.
Then place a poultice on the area, and bind it, and leave it until all the remaining water flows out: then treat it until the wound heals.
If however the opposition is to the flow of water when you pierce it: and this is not due to anything but that the white membrane causes opposition at the opening of the wound, and prevents the exit of water: then it is necessary to insert a pen into the wound, or an instrument with which water is extracted from dropsical patients, whose form has been mentioned previously: or add in the operation of the wound for a moment.
And you should know that the water returns and accumulates after six months, or around that time. When it therefore accumulates, then it should be punctured according to the same method, and the patient will spend his days.
Chapter LXIII.
Regarding the treatment of fleshy rami.
Know that in the cutting of this ramus, there is great fear leading to peril in many conditions. Therefore, it seems to me that its dismissal is salvaging from it.
And I am recalling the procedure on it and the appearance of the abscess.
I say therefore, that many abscesses occur in the bodies from which the testicles are composed: and it happens for various reasons, namely.
Or from acute or sharp excess that is discharged toward the testicles. Or from percussion.
And the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body, and no pain is found in it: and it is a heavy abscess.
And perhaps it is a stony abscess, whose color is dark, and it has no sensation.
And sometimes it occurs from the knotting of the arteries and their swelling: as has already been mentioned beforehand: or from the swelling of the veins.
That which is among them due to the swelling of the arteries is recognized by the nature of the abscess when you press it with your fingers. And you should not touch it at all.
That which occurs from the swelling of the veins does not disperse anything upon compression with the fingers.
And now it is possible that a section may be made on this type and on the other flesh: and it is as if you were to cut the skin of the testicles. Then extend the egg upward, and extract it with a white ligature: and free the suspensory ligament from the vessels, and tie the vessels: and cut the suspensory ligament after you free it from all parts of the egg.
If the egg is solidly attached to the flesh that has grown, then you must pull the egg and cut it.
And if there is an adhesion between some part of the ligature or what is between the vessels: then you must free that entire adhesion and cut it with a circular incision.
If there is flesh growth in the area of adhesion that is behind: then you must cut all of it and extract the egg, as we have said.
When therefore your operation is completed, then fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine: then care for it with the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
Chapter LXIIII.
On the care of shoots, which is with vines.
It is a swelling of the testicles enclosed by a kind of folding, similar to a bag, with softening of the testicles: and it makes movement, exercise, and walking difficult for the patient.
And in the treatment of this illness, there is fear, because of what has been previously mentioned.
However, we must speak of the treatment for it according to what the first practitioners did.
I say, therefore, that the patient should be made to sit on an elevated seat. Then push the suspensory ligament of the testicles downward. Then hold the skin of the testicles with your fingers, near the roots: and let another assistant hold and stretch them forcefully.
Then make a transverse incision with a broad and sharp scalpel directly on the vessels until the vessels are exposed.
Then scrape from all sides as we have told you in the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.
Then insert a needle with double thread into them, and tie it at the first place where the vines are affected: and tie it again at the last place. Then cut it in a straight section through the middle according to the length of the body, and extract what accumulates from corrupted feculent humidities.
Then treat the wound with the treatment of other wounds, in which pus is generated, so that the vessels nourishing one of the testicles fall. For it is not evil through that.
If, however, the Vitis affects all the vessels, then it is necessary to remove the testicles along with the vessels: so that the egg is not deprived of nourishment due to the incision, and waste away or dry up, and not be beneficial with them.
Chapter LXV.
Regarding the treatment of intestinal branches.
The outcome of this branching is from the incision that occurs in the sifach extended over the abdomen in the groin area from the mirach of the belly.
Therefore, the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles. And this rupture is either from the sifach or its extension.
And these two types occur from many causes: either from a blow, or jumping, or shouting, or lifting a heavy object, and similar actions.
And the sign is when it is from the extension of the sifach. It occurs gradually over a long period of time and does not happen suddenly: and it is an abscess equal toward the depths: therefore, the sifach compresses the intestine.
And its sign when it is from the cutting of the intestine, because it causes to happen from the beginning of itself a sudden intense pain: and it is a different abscess, appearing under the skin nearby: and that is due to the exit of the intestines, and their course to the exterior of the intestine.
And sometimes it exits with the intestine twisted: and this is called Intestinal Ramex, and twisting: and sometimes it occurs with gas.
And sometimes the feces run into the intestine and are retained there: and it is harmful to the patient: for it causes a bad pain, especially when it is pressed.
And in the treatment of this type of illness with iron there is fear: therefore one must be careful of accidents in it.
And the method of the operation is to instruct the patient to return the intestine with his own hand to the inner cavity, if it obeys the return. Then he should lie on his back between your hands: and raise his legs.
Then extend the skin that follows up to the higher area, and cut all the skin of the testicles along their length. Then insert hooks into the two lips of the incision according to what is needed to open the incision with them: and the incision should be of such quantity that it is possible for the egg to come out of it.
Then remove the outer layer of sifak and what is under the skin of the testicles until the white, hard sifak is revealed on all sides: then insert your index finger into what follows the testicle, between the white sifak that is under the egg's skin, and between the second sifak, and separate with it the adhesion that is at the back part of the egg.
Then move with the right hand the skin of the testicles towards the inside: and at the same time extend the white saph with the left hand upwards: and lift up the egg with the saph to the cutting part: and command the assistant to extend the egg upwards: and you release the adherence which is behind after complete separation.
And feel with your fingers that there is nothing there of the intestine wrapped in the hard white saph. If you find anything of it: then push it down towards the abdomen.
