Then take a needle with thick thread, made of linen from ten threads: and insert it through the last saph, that is, the tunic, which is under the skin of the testicles following the cut: then cut the ends that protrude from the thread until there are four strands. Then arrange some of them over some in the shape of a cross: and tie them with the saph we mentioned, which is under the skin of the testicles with a very strong ligament, until none of the vessels that nourish them can send anything to them: so that a warm aposteme does not result from it. And place another ligature outside the first ligature, less than two fingers away from it. And after these two ligatures, release from the saph which is under the skin of the testicles a quantity equal to the size of a finger: and cut the rest entirely following the round shape, and remove the egg from it.
Then cut in the lower part of the testicles' skin where blood and pus flow, as we have mentioned before.
Then apply wool soaked in oil, and place it on the wound: and apply the bandage which we mentioned. And sometimes the white sifach that we mentioned is cauterized after its incision, fearing the flow of blood. For it often happens. And remove the bandage, until it falls off by itself.
If however its falling off is delayed, then it should be soaked with warm water: and place on it what we said, until it falls off.
Then treat the wound with the rest of the treatment for wounds, until it is healed.
Chapter LXVI.
Regarding the windy arm.
In this windy arm, I have not seen anyone who dared to attempt its treatment with iron.
And the first ones said that it occurs as we have mentioned in the arm that is with the vine. Which is to bind the vessels after cutting and easily apply something over them: then cut in the middle, and finally treat it with what opens it, until the vessels fall off: and treat the wound as we have said, until it heals.
Chapter LXVII.
Regarding the rupture that occurs in the groin.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and the area protrudes, and nothing from the intestines descends to the testicles: and if it does descend, it is only a little and returns at all times: but if time is prolonged with it, a fissure is added in the sifach, until the intestines descend into the sifach.
And it happens from the stretching of the sifach, which is in the groin, as we said. Which is because the sifach is stretched; then it softens, and the area becomes inflamed and protrudes.
And its treatment is with cautery, as was previously narrated.
And sometimes it is treated with an iron, according to this method: and it is that the patient lies on their back under your hands. Then cut the swollen and protruding area of the rupture with a horizontal cut, according to the width of three fingers.
Then grasp the alsifak and what is beneath the skin until the white sifach is revealed, which is under the skin that follows it.
Then take the probe and place it on the protruding area of the sifach, and press it deeply into the abdomen.
Then sew the two protruding areas on the end of the probe from the sifach together with a suture; then remove the end of the probe.
And do not cut the alsifach at all, nor stretch the egg, nor anything else, as I made you know in the treatment of intestinal ramus.
Then treat it with the treatment for wounds. Therefore, when you cut the threads, clean it and heal the wound until it is healed.
For the sifach contracts, and does not add to the protrusion of the rupture.
And the cautery is better in this place: for it is nearer to safety.
Chapter LXVIII.
On the softening of the skin of the testicles.
The skin of the testicles is often softened in some men, because of which the flesh between them is also softened, and its appearance is marred.
Therefore, it is necessary for the one who is asked to treat it to make the patient lie on his back and cut away all the softened skin down to the natural skin.
Then bring together the two lips with a suture: and if you wish, first remove the excess of the softened skin with three or four stitches, and secure the suture firmly.
Then cut between the sutures.
Then treat it as you would other wounds until it heals, and the threads fall out.
Chapter LXIX.
On Castration.
Know that castration is excommunicated in our law: and because of this, it would be permissible for me not to mention it in my book: and there is no need to mention it, except for two methods.
One of which is that it should be known by the doctor when asked about it: and so that he may know its treatment if it happens to someone.
The other reason is that we often need the castration of certain animals for our benefit through it, such as rams, goats, and cats, and similar animals.
I say therefore, that castration is done in two ways. Or by rubbing. Or by incision and cutting.
In that which is done by rubbing, the way of the operation is: that we make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles soften and relax and hang down; then rub them with your hand until they dissolve and do not appear under touch.
In castration by incision and cutting, it is necessary to hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then ligate the suspensorium, and cut above all the egg with one cut, until when two eggs come out: then incise them after you have defleshed each, and do not leave anything on them except a fine suture over the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than the one done by rubbing: because rubbing may leave some part of the testicles, whereby the animal lacks desire for copulation.
Then care for the wound until it heals.
Chapter LXX.
Regarding the treatment of hermaphrodites in two methods.
Hermaphroditism in males occurs in two ways. One of them is that there appears between the testicles or on the skin of the testicles, in the area between the two testicles, a figure like the vulva of a woman, with hair: and sometimes urine flows from that which is on the skin of the testicles.
In women, however, there is one type, and it is the woman's womb above the comb like the small male testicles, protruding to the outside: of which one is like the male priapus, and two like the two testicles.
And the treatment for the three types, two from men, and one type from women, is: because it is necessary to cut the added flesh until the impression of them disappears. Then treat them with the treatment of other wounds.
In the second type of men, from which urine exits, which is in the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is there any treatment for it at all.
Chapter LXXI.
Regarding the incision of tentigine, and the protruding flesh in women's wounds.
Tentigo perhaps is added above the natural part, until it becomes disfigured and its appearance is ugly: and sometimes it is enlarged in some women so much that it expands like in men, and extends to the act of intercourse.
Therefore, you should hold the excess of the tentigo with your hand or with a hook, and cut it: and do not be hasty in the incision, especially at the root: so that blood flow does not occur.
Then treat it with the treatment of wounds until it heals.
The arisen flesh is the flesh that grows in the opening of the womb until it fills it: and it perhaps extends to the outside resembling a tail: and because of this, some first call the ailment tailed. Therefore, we must incise it as we incise a tentigo, and treat it until it heals.
On the treatment of Alratica, which is an unperforated female ulcer.
Chapter LXXII.
Alratica is an unperforated female ulcer, or a small opening. And it is either natural or accidental.
Accidental ulcers arise from a preceding illness: they may form either from added flesh growth, or if fine and thin, or thick: they can occur either in the depth of the matrix, or on its sides, or on its upper part, or lower part: and they prevent intercourse and impregnation, and childbirth, and may also prevent menstruation.
And its diagnosis is made by the observation of the midwife, if evident swelling is nearby.
If it is not apparent, then seek it with your fingers, or with a probe.
If the swelling is from a fine substance and is close to the two lips, then act quickly and rupture it.
And it is done by placing small particles on the two lips.
Then place the index fingers of both your hands simultaneously, and let the woman lie on her back with her legs spread apart. Then extend the two lips with force until the fine substance is ruptured and the swelling is opened.
Then take wool, and soak it in oil, and place it on the area: and the woman should come every day, so that the area does not become solidified by something else.
If however the sifach is thick, dense: then it is necessary to cut it with a broad spatula similar to a myrtle leaf.
If however the excrescence is from flesh grown, then suspend it with hooks, and cut it: and let there be with you medicines that stop the flow of blood without clotting, such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and frankincense compounded with egg white.
Then administer a large cannula of lead, so that the wound does not solidify quickly, keep it for several days: and apply lint from dry linen, then treat with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
And sometimes other flesh growths originate in the womb: therefore they must be cut according to this method: for it is not a cancerous abscess; no opposition should be made with iron at all for a cancerous abscess that is in the womb.
Chapter LXXIII.
Concerning the treatment of hemorrhoids, Athehelil, and red Bothor in women's wounds.
Hemorrhoids are the opening of vein orifices, through which a great deal of blood flows continuously.
When therefore hemorrhoids become old, they turn into thelil: and I have already spoken about their types and signs in the division: and here I will say which of them receive healing, and which do not.
I say therefore, that hemorrhoids which are in the opening of the womb, and do not appear to the sense: then there is no treatment for them with iron.
But those which are in the opening of the womb, on which the sense falls, are those that can be treated.
Therefore, it is necessary to put the woman in a cold house. Then extend the athehelil with scissors, or with a coarse cloth, and cut them from their roots.
Then powder over them at the flow of blood from one of the powders of lancing without mordancy: such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and frankincense, and similar to them.
Then push her feet against the wall for one hour. Then place her in cold water.
If the flow of blood persists: then have her sit in a decoction of sumac, and pomegranate peel, and gallnuts, and similar items.
Then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it on her back.
If therefore the blood is constricted with it, it is good: and if not, make blisters adhere to the back without scarification.
Then take wool, and soak it in the juice of tarathit, or the juice of arnoglossae, or the juice of alaulat branches, that is, agrimony, with Pontic wine, and make it adhere to the site.
When therefore the abscess rests, then treat the place with ointments, until it is healed.
Albart however is similar to the heads of alhass, and it has a rough appearance.
Therefore, you must cut what appears from it, according to what I said in thethil equally: and treat it until it is healed.
Chapter LXXIV.
Regarding the perforation of the uterus that occurs in the matrix.
Many kinds of abscesses occur in the uterus, such as cancer, and stone abscess, and ulcers, and adubelati, and alekilati, that is, herpes, aestiomemus, and fistulas, and hemorrhoids, and ragadiae, and thelil, and hot abscess.
And I have indeed already spoken of all these diseases and their kinds, and their signs, and their cures in the division: it is necessary that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess which occurs in the uterus, when it is among those abscesses which collect pus, and you wish to know how its opening is made with an iron.
Therefore, you must consider. Then if the pain of the abscess at its onset is sharp with its throbbing, and flame, and fever: and you see it redden: if sensation falls upon it, then do not hasten with its perforation: and treat it with what aids maturation until the acuteness of the symptoms subsides.
Then it is necessary that you make the woman sit on a seat that has two supports, and let her recline, or lie down on her back, and gather her feet toward the lower part of her belly: and her thighs should be spread apart, and she places her arms under her knees, and bind each with a suitable ligature.
Then the midwife should sit on the right side and administer the instrument with which the opening of the womb is widened.
And it is necessary when you wish to administer this instrument, that you insert with the sound the depth of the woman's womb: so that what enters from the instrument is not more than the depth of the womb, and injure the patient.
If the instrument is longer than the depth, then it is necessary to place small objects on the covering of the womb's depth: so that the entire instrument is prevented from entering into the depth of the womb: and it is necessary to place the spiral, which runs in the instrument, from the upper side: and to hold the instrument, and for the assistant to turn the spiral until the depth of the womb is opened.
When therefore the exitura appears and is touched by hand, and it is soft and tender: then it is necessary to cut it at its head with a broad spatula.
When therefore the pus is evacuated, then it is necessary to place on the wound a lint that has been soaked in rose oil: or green oil, which has some astringency: and place the lint, and remove the section from the depth of the womb.
And place externally on the womb, and on the comb clean wool soaked in water, in which sloes have been boiled.
Then it should be treated after two days with an ointment that is suitable for it, until it heals.
And sometimes the womb and the wound are washed by being irrigated with water and honey: then with water in which the root of lily or long aristolochia has been boiled: then return to the ointment.
If the wound is hidden inside the womb, then you must abstain from treating it with iron, but rather treat it with what we have said in the division.
Chapter LXXIV.
Teaching on obstetrics, how to treat live embryos that have been expelled in an unnatural form.
It is necessary for the obstetrician to know first the natural form of childbirth.
The signs of this are that when you see a woman compressed in the lower parts, and she desires to breathe air, and is relieved by what is on her from the labor, and the exit of the embryo is hastened: then you know that this birth is according to the natural form, and its exit is head first, with the afterbirth following; or suspended, or hanging from the navel.
Therefore, when you see these signs, then it is necessary to compress her belly so that the embryo descends quickly.
For when it descends head first, the afterbirth descends with it, and it is cleansed of those excesses by good cleansing.
Whoever is beyond this birth is unnatural, praiseworthy not.
For sometimes the fetus exits over its feet, and its body comes out before its head, and one of its feet or hand; or its head and hand come out; or it exits as a breech: and it may turn onto its neck, and similar praiseworthy figures.
It is therefore necessary for the obstetrician to be wise and subtle in all these matters and beware of error and deception: and I am showing every figure among them, and how the method in it is, and what it signifies, and stand by it.
When the fetus exits with its head in its natural exit, and it becomes severe for the woman, and the labor becomes difficult for her, and you see that her strength is now weakened: then make her sit on a seat, or let women hold her: and fumigate her vagina with fenugreek decoction, and with moist oils.
Then the midwife should insert a small spatula between her fingers, and tear open the amnion with it, and cut it with her nail until the moisture inside flows out: and press the woman's belly until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, then the woman must be purged with a mucilage of fenugreek and with sesame oil.
Then command her after the purge to be compressed: and make her sneeze with spices, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour. For the fetus will exit immediately.
If two hands of the fetus come out first, you must gradually and easily return them. If it does not obey at the entrance, then place the woman on a seat and lift her feet upwards: then shake the seat on the ground: and the woman should be held so she does not fall during the shaking.
If therefore the hands do not come out and the fetus dies: then cut them and extract the remainder of the fetus: and tie its hand with a cloth, and extract it evenly: for it will come out.
The exit of the embryo over its feet. When the fetus comes out feet first, then it is necessary to push them upwards: then gradually turn the fetus: then align it.
Then take one of its feet and gradually extend it.
When they come out up to the thighs, then command her to compress and make her sneeze with condiments: for it will come out, if God wills.
And if it does not come out with what we have mentioned, then gradually return the fetus until you place it according to its natural form. For it will then come out with an easy exit.
If it is prevented despite all that we have mentioned: then take some marshmallow mucilage, linseed oil, and dissolved gum: and pound everything well in a mortar: then anoint her womb and the lower part of her abdomen with it. Then make her sit in warm water until she achieves hypochondria.
When therefore you see that her lower parts are heated, then make for her a sieve of myrrh: and place it. When therefore she holds the sieve for one hour, then make her sit on the seat. Then make her sneeze: and hold her mouth and nose: and press the lower part of the abdomen with a gentle pressure. For the fetus will come out immediately.
The exit of the fetus is over the thighs and hands. When it exits in this manner, then she will gradually introduce her hands. Then the woman should lie back on her neck, and let her feet hang down below: and she should be lying on the bed, and fold her hands. Then press on her abdomen gradually. Then remove what is under her feet from the pillows until she is prepared on the lower part. If the fetus does not come out, then take her feet, and move them with a vigorous motion. Then press what is above the hypochondrium gradually until the fetus ascends to the upper parts. Then she should insert her hands and gradually adjust the fetus: and instruct the woman to compress herself until the fetus exits.
The fetus hanging transversely exiting from the hands. He will devise in the reduction of his hand. If he cannot reduce it, then lift the woman and make her walk.
If she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed and shake her legs violently.
Then apply the liniment that you have prepared from emollients.
If labor begins for her, then make her sit on a seat. Then attend to the reduction of the hand, and align the fetus according to its natural position: and make the woman sneeze, and command her to compress herself until it exits.
The fetus exiting over its neck, with hands spread out, and its face is toward the back of its mother. The midwife must hold the hand of the fetus, then gradually revolve it and align it with ease.
When it is aligned, then place on its mouth what we have mentioned made from oil and emollients.
Then command her to move gradually. When you have done that, then make her sit on a seat and command her to lean to the right side. Then command her to compress herself and make her sneeze with you preparing.
The prepared fetus is removed onto the side. When it descends to the opening of the matrix in this way with the afterbirth, then tear the afterbirth with your nail until it is emptied of moisture.
If it is suspended over the face of the fetus and its neck, then cut it from the navel so that it does not remain and cause death.
Then push the fetus inward until you place it as is proper: and instruct the woman to bear down several times: for it will come out with a slight effort.
The delivery of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins are often born: and sometimes three, and four are born. However, that is unusual, and rarely happens.
Five is beyond nature, and they do not live at all: and a single afterbirth contains them, although they multiply, and are separated by a siphon, distinguishing the tied cord of each of them at the navel.
And sometimes they exit like a single fetus does in a natural, easy delivery: and they exit in an undesirable manner, as we have described.
If some of them are difficult during childbirth and come to what we have mentioned about unnatural positions, then care for them as we have described: and let a skilled midwife be present, who acts with ease and caution, and adapts herself to every position according to the skill that leads to their safety.
A reminder of what is formed in the womb from embryos and aborts.
Sometimes one is formed in the womb, and two, and three, and four, and five, and six, and seven, and more than ten: and it has already been verified by me that a woman aborted and expelled seven, and another fifteen, all fully formed.
Which was done by the measurement of the glorious wise man.
Therefore, all of this must be known by the obstetrician. For perhaps it may come to her like that case; therefore, she should apply what is appropriate to it.
Chapter LXXVI.
Regarding the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you treat a dead fetus with what I have said in the division on medication, and it does not come out, and you are forced to use manual operation, then you must take care.
If therefore the woman is of sound health, and is not affected by any accidents from which danger to her is feared: then it is necessary that the woman lie on her back on a bed, with her head inclined downwards, and her legs raised: and an attendant should hold her on both sides, or she should be tied to the bed, so that her body is not pulled out during the extraction of the fetus.
Then moisten the mouth of the womb with moist oils and with the mucilage of althea, fenugreek, and flaxseed.
Then the midwife should anoint her hand with these oils and jellies; then she should insert it into the womb with ease. Then she should seek with it the place where she can fix the hooks to the fetus and suitable places for that.
Consider then if the fetus is prepared to descend head first: then fix the hooks in its eyes, or in its neck, or in its mouth, or in its palate, or under its chin, or in its clavicle, or in places close to the ribs, and under the hypochondria.
If, however, the descent is feet first, then in its pubic region and in its middle ribs.
And it is necessary that she hold the hook with her right hand: and place its curvature between the fingers of her left hand: and insert it with ease, and fix the hook in one of those places we mentioned, until she reaches the empty space.
Then she should fix another hook opposite it, or a third if needed: so that the contraction is equal, and does not lean to one side.
Then it should be extended with equal extension, and the extension should not be only straight, but moved in all directions to ease its exit: as is done with a tooth during its extraction.
And it is necessary that between those parts, the extension be softened. If a part is retained, then the midwife should anoint some fingers with oil and insert them from one side to turn back what is retained.
If therefore a part of the fetus comes out, then change the hooks to a higher place: do this until the entire fetus comes out.
If therefore the hand comes out first and it is not possible to reduce it due to its constriction: then it is necessary that a cloth be wrapped over it. Then extract it until it comes out entirely, cut it either at the ankle joint or at the elbow: and so you must do for the other hand, and for both feet.
If however the fetus's head is large, or it encounters constriction upon exit, or there is water gathered in its head: then it is necessary to insert a spathile with spikes between the fingers, and split the head with it, and extract the water: or break it with an instrument called Almisdac: whose form comes with the forms of the other instruments in the chapter that follows this.
Similarly do if the fetus is of a large head nature, then it is necessary to cut with an algengematu: or extract it with a misdach, as we have said. Then attract the bones with forceps.
If the head comes out and is constricted at the fork: then it should be split until the moisture in the chest is released.
If however it does not untangle and does not obey the exit: then cut the head piece by piece, according to what is possible for you.
If the lower part of the belly is abscessed, or there is dropsy in it: then it is necessary to pierce it until the moisture runs out.
If however the fetus is on its feet, then its extraction is easy, and its direction to the maternal orifice is light.
If however it is constricted at the abdomen or chest, then you must extract it with a cloth which you have wrapped over your hand, and cut open the abdomen or chest until what is inside comes out.
If however the other limbs are removed and the head returns, then the midwife should insert her left hand. If therefore the maternal orifice is open, then she should insert her hand deeply into the womb and seek with it the head, and pull it with her fingers up to the maternal orifice: then insert one hook or two hooks into it, and pull it with them.
If the maternal orifice is constricted due to a warm swelling that has occurred in it, then one should not labor over it; rather, at that time, one should apply liquid and fatty substances, and administer plasters: and sit in waters that soften and moisten.
If the fetus is on its side, then it is possible for it to be aligned: then what we have said for a living fetus should be administered.
If it is not possible to do that, then it should be cut piece by piece and extracted.
And it is necessary that you do not leave anything of the afterbirth inside at all.
When therefore you have completed your operation, then administer what we have said for warm swellings that occur in the wombs.
If there is a flow of blood, then bathe in astringent waters and administer the rest of the treatment.
And indeed I have seen a woman whose womb contained a dead fetus; then she conceived another one over it, and later another fetus also died. It happened to her after a long time that an abscess formed on her navel, and it swelled until it opened, and began to discharge pus.
I was called to treat her, and I treated her for a long time: and the wound did not heal.
I therefore applied to it some strongly attractive plasters: and the bone came out from the site. Then after a few days, another bone came out. I was therefore amazed by this, since there is no bone in the belly.
I then thought that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
I therefore examined the wound and extracted many bones, with the woman being in better condition: and she has lived thus for a long time, and now discharges only a little pus from the site.
And I did not include this foreign matter here unless there is knowledge in it, and assistance for what the skilled physician administers with his hand in treatment.
Chapter LXXVII.
Regarding the forms of necessary instruments for the extraction of a fetus.
The form of the end by which the matrix is opened.
Here is the form of the book binder, with which books are bound, having two equal ends at the extremities of two pieces of wood. However, this end should be finer than the binder: and it is made either from ebony or from boxwood.
And the width of the entire wood should be about two fingers: and the edge of each of both is about one finger, and the length of each is a palm and a half: and in the middle of the two pieces of wood are two additional pieces of the same kind of wood, which are already fixed in both, whose length is half a palm and a little more: and the width of each is about two fingers, or a little more.
And these two additional pieces are inserted into the mouth of the matrix, so that it opens with them when you turn the two ends.
Another form similar to that one, finer and lighter.
It should be made from ebony wood or boxwood, in the shape of tongs. However, at the end of it there should be two additional pieces, as you see here above: and the length of each entire additional piece is about a palm: and the width of each is two fingers.
When you wish to open the matrix with it, then have the woman sit on the bed with her feet hanging down and what is between her legs open. Then insert those two connected additional pieces into the matrix: and you hold the lower end of the instrument between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument, as you do with scissors, equally according to the amount you wish from the opening of the mother's mouth, until the midwife does what she wants.
The other form of vertigo, which the ancients called the form of the driver, by which the fetus is driven.
The form of Almisdac, by which the large head is crushed: and it is compared to a forceps, which has teeth at the end, as you see.
And sometimes it is made elongated, like forceps according to this form, as you see, which has teeth like a saw's teeth, by which it cuts and crushes.
The form of the hook having one spine.
The form of the hook having two spines.
The form of the spatula having two ends for cutting off the head.
The form of two broad spatulas.
All these instruments are used, and the more their kinds are multiplied, and prepared by the craftsman, the faster they are for their operation, and more esteemed among people because of their quantity.
Therefore, do not disdain any of them so that it may be prepared for you. For their necessity is inexcusable.
Chapter LXXVIII.
On the extraction of the afterbirth.
When the afterbirth is retained at birth, then you must instruct the patient to hold her breath. Then make her sneeze with condisi: and place your hand over her mouth and nostrils. If it exits through this method, it is good.
If not: then take a pot and pierce a hole in the cover. Place herbs that open the womb in it, such as reed, rue, dill, chamomile, fennel, lignum aloes, and centaury. Take all these herbs or some of them, submerge them with water, and place them on fire.
Then place a reed tube over the hole in the pot's cover, and put the other end into the womb opening: and hold it until the vapor reaches the cavity of the womb.
Then make her sneeze, as we said. For the afterbirth will exit with ease.
If it remains after this treatment and does not exit: then instruct the midwife to dip her hand in sesame oil or coltsfoot mucilage. Then insert it into the womb and search for the afterbirth with it. When therefore he finds it, then let him take it and stretch it gradually.
If however it is attached deep in the womb, then let him insert his hand as we have described, until he finds the Secundina, and extract it gradually straight, so that the womb does not fall due to strong pulling: rather it must be changed with ease to the right and left sides; then add to the amount of pulling. For it obeys then, and is preserved, and escapes from adhering.
If the mouth of the womb is constricted, as we have already mentioned: treat it with sneezing and with a medicine pot with herbs.
If however it does not come out with all that we have mentioned, then beware lest you tire yourself in repeating the extraction.
But it is necessary that what comes out to the mouth of the womb from it, you tie to the woman's thigh. Then cleanse her with an ointment of tetrapharmacum. For it will腐烂后天，溶解并排出。
However when it putrefies, a bad smell rises to the stomach and head, and it harms the weak one. Therefore, appropriate fumigations should be administered for that.
Some of the ancients have already experienced the fumigation of mustard and dried figs.
The form of the instrument used for fumigating a woman during the retention of afterbirth and menses.
Let it be made from a container similar to alcama, or from horn: and let the wider end be placed over fire: and the fumigation should be positioned over coals: hold it until that fumigation is consumed: and repeat with another.
Chapter LXXIX.
Regarding the treatment of an unperforated anus.
Many children are born with their anus not perforated, which has already been covered by a thin membrane. Therefore, the midwife should pierce it with her finger: and if not, pierce it with a sharp spatula: and she should be careful of the muscle, so as not to touch it.
Then place wool soaked in wine and oil on it. Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
If you fear it may close up, then place a lead tube in the opening for many days, and remove it when the child needs to defecate.
And it also happens that the anus becomes obstructed due to the healing of a wound or an abscess. Therefore, that consolidation must be cut, then it should be treated with what we have said about treatment and lead.
Chapter LXXX.
On the treatment of fistulas that occur in the lower part.
Fistulas that occur in the lower part are Nodulation and Swelling that happen near the anus externally: or in the space of one region: and it is one Fistula or multiple.
When that nodulation becomes old, it opens, and a watery white moisture or fine pus runs from it.
And sometimes these fistulas are penetrating. Therefore, penetrating fistulas are recognized by what exits with discharge and flatulence when the patient has a bowel movement: and perhaps worms may exit from them.
And there are fistulas among them when they are in the space penetrating all the way to the bladder and to the urethra. And there are those that penetrate all the way to the hip joint and to the coccyx.
From which it is known that a penetrating fistula extends to the anus, as opposed to a non-penetrating one, is by inserting your index finger into the anus and inserting a thin probe made of air or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
If there is a twist in it, then insert into it a thin lead probe or a hair from horse's tail until you feel the probe or the hair with your finger.
If you do not feel it thoroughly, and nothing comes out of the opening from discharge, nor gas, nor worm as I said: then know that it is not penetrable: therefore hurry to the treatment.
And when the fistula penetrates to the bladder or to the urethra: then its indication is the discharge of urine from it, and the prevention of consolidation of the area with medicines.
If it penetrates to the hip joint or to the hip bone: then its sign is that the probe reaches there, if there is no twist until the bone: and the discovery of pain around the part, and that pus comes out of it always: and that treatment is not effective, nor does it consolidate with ointment.
And in all these penetrating fistulas there is no cure at all: and the treatment of them is labor and vanity for him, by foolish doctors, upon whom it is formed.
In that which is not penetrable and not old, healing is hoped for with a scalpel: according to what I narrate to you, and I have already tested: and it is that the patient lies in your hands on his back: and raise his legs up above his hips, and his hips are inclined towards his abdomen. Then insert a probe of lead or brass, if there is a twist in the fistula, until you know where the probe reaches.
And if the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your index finger into the anus.
If you feel that the worm has already penetrated on its own through the detected area, besides what you feel between your finger and the surface or the flesh itself, then you can be sure that it is penetrating. Therefore, do not labor over it, for there is no cure for it, as we have said.
They said, however, that the flesh is healed in some men and through the treatment in which help is hoped for, it is to ignite a fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned before, and insert the ignited cautery into the fistula until it reaches near the anus. Then do this twice or three times until you know that all those added filtered flesh, which resembles the tube of a bird's feather, have been burned.
Then treat it with linen wrapped in butter until the burned flesh comes out; then treat it with ointments that generate flesh and strengthen.
If it is healed, it is good.
And if not, then it will never be healed with any other treatment.
And if the worm comes out and does not reach your finger which is in the anus, and there is a thick veil of flesh or membrane between it and the worm: and you see the fistula following the surface of the skin, then cut the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and you go cutting with the worm that is in the fistula until the incision reaches where the end of the worm is, and the worm is freed and falls out.
Then clean those filtered meats which resemble a bird's feather tube so that nothing remains from them.
If however the blood overcomes you and separates you from your operation so that you cut those meats: then it is better and quicker to heal by cauterizing it with fire or with sharp medicine.
For the cautery with fire brings good effects, the burning of those added meats, and the cutting off of blood, and the drying of moistures.
Then treat it with linen wrapped in butter, or crushed fat, until the place emits pus, and those burned meats come out in pus.
Then treat the wound with consolidating ointments, which generate hard flesh: and there are medicines that have astringency and drying properties.
For when they are restored, then it is already healed: and you do not fear repetition.
If however the fistula has already reached deep into the anus, and extends from the excess of the body: then insert your finger into the anus, and explore with it.
If therefore you feel a tent, and between you and it there is a veil of sinew or flesh, and it is close to penetration: then there is no operation in that place unless according to the way of confidence and hope.
Which means that one of the three methods is applied to it: either you cauterize it as we have said: or you cut it until you reach its concavity, so that it is possible for you to insert a thread and perform treatment nearby. And do not proceed much with the cutting, so as not to cut the tendon containing the anus, and involuntary discharge may occur in the patient. Then treat it with what we have said.
For it may be healed: or you may retract the membrane itself, and clean it after you cut it up to near the anus, as we have said, using a probe or another instrument with a sharp end. Then clean the filtered flesh that is in the incision as far as you can with examination.
Then attempt the restoration of the entire wound with the incision, and the upper opening where it is consolidated: and the fistula remains open on the inner part of the anus, and it will be milder for the patient.
And sometimes the fistula is sewn in this manner: it is when you insert a probe into the fistula: and it is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with the skin and the edge of the anus: then take a probe with a perforated end, which is like a leather worker's needle, that is, of those who prepare hides, in this form. And insert into it a thread made from five threads wound together, and around it. Then insert the probe with the thread into the fistula until it reaches its cavity.
If it penetrates into the inner edge of the anus nearby, then withdraw the thread from that opening: so that you insert your finger into the anus and pull out the end of the thread, and bring both ends together: and hold both tightly, and leave it for one day or two days: and the more the thread cuts into the flesh, hold it firmly until the flesh between the two ends of the thread is cut and falls off: then treat the wound until it heals and consolidates.
If however the opening of the fistula is not penetrating: then make it penetrate by whichever method is prepared for you, unless it is very deep. For it is not within you to do that because of the flap, so as not to cut it.
Then do with it as we have said, until it heals.
The form of the spatumilis spinosi with which the fistula is split, whose curvature is very sharp, and the other part is not sharp, so as not to cut what is not necessary, as you see.
Chapter LXXXI.
About the suturing of hemorrhoids, from which blood runs from their incision: and the treatment of fissures.
There are hemorrhoids according to two ways. For either they are inside the anus, similar to coal sacs or ember sacs: or they are like grains of a grape. And among them there are small ones and large ones: and blood runs from them always, and there is one, and there are many. And they are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
However, those which are outside the anus, are mostly lacking in moisture, from which yellow water or a little blood runs continuously: and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of that which is inside the anus is to advise the patient to sit: and to be expressed until the anus protrudes, and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Therefore hang with hooks: or hold them with your nail. Then cut them at their roots.
If however the hooks do not hold in them because of their moisture and softness: then take them with a coarse cloth, or with woolen mittens made of felted wool, and extract them with your fingers. Then cut them, and sprinkle on them after the cutting certain hot powders, so that they may serve as a substitute for cauterization. Or cauterize them according to what was precedented in the chapter on cauterizing. Then care for them with the rest of the treatment until they heal.
If the anus does not obey the call to evacuate, then give the patient an enema that contains a slight irritant, so that it cleanses what is inside the anus and obeys the call to evacuate quickly when the patient exerts himself.
If however the growths are external to the anus, then their treatment is easy and simple: it is as you take them with your nail, or you take them with a hook, and cut them. Then care for them with what we have said until they heal.
And for those who shrink from cutting with iron, then it is necessary to administer their stitching according to this method. Take the wrapped thread and insert it into the needle. Then pull the growth upward, and make it penetrate with the needle at its root from the other side: and wrap both ends of the thread around the lower part of the needle, and let them be horizontal: and bind the growth with a strong tie. Then tie the thread, and draw out the needle.
Do this with all the athelil, and leave one of them untouched: do not sew it up, so that the excess blood may flow out from it.
Then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or cerote over the anus, and put it on the anus: and instruct the patient to rest. Then leave it until it falls off.
When the athelil fall off, care for them with ointments and the rest of the treatment until they heal.
On the Treatment of Fissures. For they often occur from the dryness of the stool and the constriction of the bowels.
When they become old and medicine does not heal them, then it is necessary to scrape them with the point of a spatula or with your nail until they become moist, and remove the outer layer that prevents their healing. Then care for them until they heal as necessary.
If they do not heal, then scrape them more forcefully than before until they bleed significantly, and remove the outer layer; then care for them until they heal.
On the Treatment of Inverted and Non-inverted Almirmar, and Dry Athelil, and Ants.
Chapter LXXXII.
You know that Almirmar is nothing but a round knot according to the color of the body, similar to the head of a nail: and it occurs throughout the whole body, especially in the lower parts of the feet, and the digits: and pain occurs from them during walking.
Therefore, what is around the nail should be cut, and it should be held with scissors, or with a hook, and pulled out from its root.
Then care for it: and if you wish, cauterize it according to what was precedented in its chapter.
From dry athelil, however, there is a small prominence, rough, filtered, round on the surface of the body. And they often occur in the hands of children.
And the treatment of it is to stretch the athelil, and cut it: or bind it with silk thread: or with hair, until it falls out. And if you wish, cauterize it according to what was mentioned with fire, or with sharp medicine: and now the athelil are extracted, both inverted and not inverted, with an instrument that I shall describe.
Formica is also a small, filtered, thick prominence on the surface of the body, going very deep: and when cold encounters it, it feels like an ant bite, and it occurs throughout the whole body: and most often it appears on the hands.
And the treatment of it is to take a tube from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather: and place that tube over the Formica, until the circle of the tube contains parts of it. Then turn your hand with the cannula until you cut what is around the Ant: and place it in the depth of the flesh, and root out the Ant from its root.
And if you wish, do it with a cannula of brass or iron, according to this form.
Let the upper part of the cannula be drawn out to a hollow point, so that the grasp upon the finger and its turning may be easier.
And if you wish to cauterize the Ant, do it according to what has been mentioned regarding the cauterization of Athelil in the chapter on the cautery.
Chapter LXXXIII.
Concerning the forms of instruments used for enemas in illnesses of the anus, and for relieving the bowels, and colic.
Sometimes an enema is made of silver, or brass, or cast metal, or hammered metal.
And sometimes these instruments are made small and large according to their use.
Therefore, that which is used in the treatment of small children should be small: and for those whose anuses are weak or painful, their enemas should be so as well.
Large enema.
Its tube, that is, the upper head where the bag is tied, should be wide according to this manner: and it should have a separation so that the bag can be tied as you see, and its lower end which is inserted into the anus should be closed, that is, not open, very soft, drawing to fineness: and on one side of it there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole.
And let the width of the hole be according to the thickness of the rays, and a little thicker, and let there be a container in which medicines are placed from an animal's bladder: or from sheep's parchment, which should be in the form of a small asofrati: whose root is one palm.
And let it be pierced with many holes as it revolves, and let the space which is between each hole be the thickness of a finger. Then insert into those holes strong thread made of raw fiber, which should be from ten threads, or around that number, and attach it to the container like a small asofrati. When the container is placed in it, it should be tied tightly at the head of the enema between two distinguishing constrictions. Then administer the enema with it.
And this is the form of the circle and the holes of the container depicted here.
The quality of administering the enema with it is: to fill the container or bladder with medicine that is warmed according to the quantity tolerable by the patient: and be careful that it is not too hot or too cold.
Then the patient should lie on their back, and raise their legs upwards: and place under them a mattress, that is, skin or cloth on which people lie, or a linen sheet.
Then anoint the end of the enema with oil, or with sheep's fat, or with fenugreek mucilage, or similar substances. Then insert it into the anus with ease. Then let the assistant take the bag with both his hands at once, and squeeze it vigorously until he empties everything that is in the clyster into the intestine.
Then remove the clyster, and let the patient raise his legs to the wall.
If the medicine forces it to exit, then he should hold as much as he can. And if he sleeps with it all night, it is more ultimate in healing.
If you give him a clyster for diarrhea-related illnesses and its discharge is rapid: then repeat the clyster until he is healed.
If there are hemorrhoids or painful abscesses in the anus, then let the clyster be very fine and mild, such as those with which children are given clysters.
And this should be the form of a fine clyster for which the skin is tight.
Chapter LXXXIV.
I have already said in the division about the treatment of wounds what was appropriate for the book, and I will now speak here about their treatment with manual methods and with medicines according to completeness.
I say therefore that wounds differ according to the instrument by which they are inflicted, and according to the place on which the wound falls.
The things by which wounds are inflicted are often, for example, the throwing of a stone, or the cutting of a sword or dagger, or the striking with a lance, wood, or arrow, and similar things from many other objects.
Wounds however that are made according to the places of the body are, such as a wound that falls upon the head, or neck, or chest, or abdomen, or spleen: and similar from those members.
And I am narrating the treatments of some wounds, so that I may set down that reasoning and rule for other wounds.
And I will begin with simple wounds of the head: because the discussion of compound wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
I therefore say. When a simple wound occurs on the head, and there is no fracture of the bone: then consider if it is from the投掷的石头或其他类似物，仅破裂了皮肤：如果伤口很大，你担心可能会发生热性脓肿：那么要迅速行动，并立即放头静脉血：不要延迟这个过程：根据其体力状况抽取适量的血液：如果没有禁止放血的情况，特别是如果从伤口流出的血液很少。 And let the bloodletting be from the opposite side of the wounded part.
And let the bloodletting be from the opposite side of the wounded part. And let the patient beware of excess, and wine, and heavy foods.
If however something prohibits bloodletting, then let it be reduced by food, and do not approach meats, nor wines.
And place on the wound, if a hot abscess occurs, a cloth soaked in rose oil alone, or with wine that has astringent properties.
If however you are safe from a warm abscess then place upon the wound if it is new with its own blood and has not changed it by air the powder which I will tell about shortly and if it has already changed by air then place upon it some ointments until it heals.
If however the wound is large or is from a sword cut and similar: and its lips do not come together with small pins then bring them together with stitches according to what I will tell about in wounds of the belly concerning their stitching.
If however the wound is already separated from the bone and hangs and there is no retention of it except with a small suspension then cut it. Then treat the wound with medicines and restore hard flesh in place of skin and instruct the patient to nourish themselves with foods that are thick such as heads and cooked wheat until it is like porridge and things similar to these.
If you find putrefaction in the skin and it does not adhere to the bone: then cut out all the putrefied part and discard it: then treat it.
If however in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flows: and it is not stopped by medicines, then apply something over the artery. If therefore you find it uncut, then cut it with a scalpel, or tie it off. If necessity requires it and what we have said does not work, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped.
If however these wounds are small, simple, then their matter is easy, light: so that you powder on them this powder: because it strengthens them before the air changes them.
Method of the flesh-forming powder. Take one part of frankincense, and two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of non-extinguished lime: grind all thoroughly, and sieve it: and fill the wound with it, and bind it tightly, until it adheres well to it, and coagulates with the blood.
Then bind it above with bandages, and leave it, and do not loosen it as long as it remains, so that it does not become inflamed. For the medicine should not be removed until it is healed.
And sometimes lime alone does this, when you do not have frankincense present, and dragon's blood also performs the same operation on many large wounds, when it is appropriate to place it on them and bind them, and the wounds are fresh with their own blood, which has not been altered by the air.
If the air has already altered them in some way, especially when it is during the summer season, then this powder's purpose is not applicable: therefore, care for it with what we have said, so that you place some digestive ointments on them: or place upon them poultices made from barley flour, made with water and honey, until they discharge pus. Then care for it with the remaining treatment until it is healed.
If however a fracture in the bone occurs with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with plasters: and I will now speak of the treatment of head fractures in what is to come.
Of wounds to the neck.
If a wound occurs on the neck, then there is no difference in treatment between it and a head wound when it is simple.
If however the nerve of the neck is already cut, or an artery: then if it is a nerve, there is no remedy for it except to treat it with things that cause strong styptic effect, such as ziniar, and zegi, and similar substances. For they harm the nerves and contract them.
And you shall not apply anything cold at all on the wound: for the substance of the nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is higher than other members: and let that with which it is cured be mild from medicines, such as lime washed several times with sweet water and mixed with oil, or with rose oil, and tutia, when it is also washed with sweet water: and other mineral stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
If the wound is large, then administer sutures: or bind its edges with linen bands. Then treat it until it heals.
If the wound has depth, or a sinus has formed in its lower part where pus has already collected, then pierce it at the most depressed place in it.
If an artery has already been cut in the wound and its flow of blood has begun: then separate or cut it, and ligate it: or cauterize it, if necessity requires it.
If however the thyroid cartilage has already been cut, either entirely, and the vocal cords are saved: then approximate the skin edges with sutures over the windpipe, and do not touch the trachea, rather level it off, and return it to its natural shape. Then bind it with a suitable bandage, and leave it for several days. Then treat it with ointments that have astringent and drying properties until it heals.
If however the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then probe it: then if there are fragments of bone in it, remove all of them, or as many as you can: and what does not prepare, leave it until the wound putrefies, and separates and its discharge is alleviated.
If the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on it the powder I have mentioned. If however bone appears in the wound and a fistula forms: then treat it with what is mentioned in its respective chapter.
Regarding wounds on spatulas.
If there is a piercing from a lance or a knife: and you see its depth, then assess. If wind or air escapes from the wound when the patient breathes heavily from it, then you know that the wound is mortal.
If it is not deep and is fresh with its blood: then do not apply powder to it from the first hour, nor bind it, so that blood does not remain in its depth and return to the heart, killing the patient: but apply a drawing ointment to it, and undo it twice a day.
If however the ointment is not present for you, then place on the wound opening an old cot, so that it may draw out what exits from its moisture: and make it so that the sick person sleeps upon the wound, so that what gathers in it may run.
If however more than three days have passed since the wound, or even more, and spasms do not occur to the sick person, nor bad palpitations of the heart, nor difficulty in breathing, and you see other conditions of theirs good: then you know that the wound is healing. Treat it therefore with licinius and the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
If however the healing of it is delayed, and it is now always open, then you know that it has become a fistula. Treat it therefore according to its chapter.
And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple on the surface of the chest or back: then treat it with what precedes from suturing, if it is large: or with powder, if it is small.
If however it has already made an impression on the bone, and fragments have come from it: then examine the wound, and hurry to remove those fragments, if they are separated. If however they are not separated, then leave them until the wound becomes putrid, for their extraction is eased.
The judgment in the treatment of other wounds occurring in other limbs is the same as what we have said.
Of wounds of the belly, and the protrusion of the intestines, and their treatment.
A rupture that occurs in the belly is major, medium, and minor.
From the major rupture, sometimes an intestine or a number of intestines protrude.
Therefore, their insertion and their suture is more forceful and difficult.
And the minor rupture also becomes difficult in another way. It follows, therefore, that their reduction is more difficult if you do not promptly return them to their place immediately: because they swell, open up, and become thickened: hence their insertion becomes difficult.
Therefore, the medium rupture is better: because with it, the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, unlike in those two types.
Know that the suture of the belly is according to four methods.
Two common sutures are used for the suture of the belly and for the suture of other wounds of the body: and two other sutures are specifically used for the other wounds. However, they are more specific to the suture of the belly: and I will tell you each one with explanation and clarification.
I say, therefore, that when the wound is small, and something of the intestine protrudes from it, and it becomes difficult to reduce it: then this is because of one of two methods. Or because of the smallness of the rupture, as we said: Or because there is swelling in the intestine due to cold air.
When therefore it is thus, then you must heat it, so that you submerge a sponge or a wet cloth in warm water alone. Or boil in water squills, and cyperus, and spike, and apply the mixture to the intestine until the swelling dissolves.
Sometimes it does that with wine which has astringency: and it is better than water alone for dissolving the swelling.
When therefore you see the swelling already dissolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which alum or mallows have been boiled. For by this its entrance is widened with a small object.
If however the return of it occurs after this treatment, then find and remove a little at the site of the rupture, with the instrument used for cutting hemorrhoids.
And the first treatment is better when prepared than surgery: and there should be no coercion to cut after necessity and lack of instruments.
Let one part of it be twisted, sharp, and the other part not sharp, and the extremity should not be as fine as that of a spatula, but rather slightly blunt: and it is that which resembles a probe, as you see.
When therefore the wound enlarges and enters the intestine, then it is necessary to reduce it to its natural form in its proper place if possible: for that is better.
When indeed there is a large rupture in the lower part of the belly: then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and place his legs higher than his head. And if it is in the upper part of the belly, then place his head and chest higher than his lower parts.
And similarly if there is a rupture in one of the two parts of the belly, then direct your attention and your consideration always to this, that the part in which the wound is should be higher than the other part.
And thus it is necessary that you administer this in large wounds and in medium wounds.
In small wounds, place it according to how it is prepared for you.
Then make sure that a faithful servant is present at your hands, who holds the entire rupture with his hand: and bring together its lips. Then reveal to the one who follows the suture bit by bit: and this is the method of a common suture.
And it is that you take a needle, or a number of needles according to the quantity of the wound's width. Then leave a distance of one finger's width from the end of the rupture, that is, the doctor's: and insert one needle along with threading it with a string at both ends of the skin, piercing through to the underlying layers with both ends until it penetrates from the other side, and you have now brought together both ends of the skin and both ends of the underlying tissue: and four rows are formed.
Then tie with a double thread around the wound several times from both sides at once until the two lips of the wound are joined by a suitable approximation.
Then measure the thickness of the finger as well, and insert another needle; then sew it with thread, just as you did with the first needle. Therefore, do not stop doing this with the needles you need until you complete the constriction of the entire wound.
And the needles should be of medium thickness between thick and thin: because very thin needles quickly penetrate the flesh: and thick ones have difficult entry into the skin: for this reason they ought to be of medium thickness.
And it should not be that the needle is fixed at both ends of the skin that are very close: so that the flesh is not cut quickly, and the wound is opened before its consolidation, and they are not stretched even with the suture, so that the wound is not prevented from consolidating.
Then cut the tips of the needles so they do not harm the patient during their sleep: and place small pieces of cloth from clothes on all sides that hold the tips of the needles: and leave them until you know that the wound is now consolidated.
And this kind of suture with needles is more suitable for small wounds. Because one needle, or two, or about that number is sufficient for their suture.
The second common suture is to join with the suture the four ends: two of the skin and two of the sifac together, with a needle on which is wound thread equal in thinness and thickness.
Then when you have penetrated with the needle these four ends, withdraw the needle from the side from which you started in the same way, so that the woven thread falls from the upper part of the wound: so it is a suture, just like the suture of cloth by which cloths are joined, and place between each suture the thickness of a little finger.
But men know this suture.
And with this suture I sewed the wound that had occurred to a man in his abdomen, who had been wounded with a dagger, and the tear of the wound was more than one palm: and about two palms had come out from the middle intestine, and there was a tear in the middle of the abdomen.
I therefore replaced it after his intestine had been outside the wound for twenty-four hours.
The wound healed in about fifteen days: and I cared for him, and he was healed: and he lived many years after that, continuing in his usual activities.
And the doctors had judged that he would not be healed.
And it was a miracle that I did not cure it with an ointment. For I was in a place where no ointment could be found, nor any of the medicines. I therefore placed an old cottoneous cloth on the wound twice a day, and continuously cleansed it with honey water until it was healed.
But I shall call two kinds of sutures proper according to the叙述的内容。
And it is that you begin with a sharp suture: and insert the needle from the outer to the inner part.
When therefore the needle penetrates the skin, and goes into the flesh according to the length and breadth of the whole body: leave the end that you inserted the needle on one side, and make it penetrate to the other end from the inner part to the outer part at the other end.
When therefore you make it penetrate, then make it penetrate according to this at the same end from the outer part to the inner: and leave the end that is on this side, and make the needle penetrate to the other end from the inner part to the outer part: and make it penetrate with your penetration as you make it penetrate in the end of the side, which is in its part, until it penetrates the whole.
Then begin again from this same side, and sew it with the end that is from the side on the other side, and withdraw the needle from the skin which it penetrated.
Then bring it back into that skin, and sew the end of the side that is on the other side with this end: and withdraw it from the skin which is on its part, and do this alternately, one after another: and do this turn by turn until you sew the entire outer part according to this example.
And the essence of this suturing is to sew the skin with a pellipariorum suture: so that you sew one side of the skin end alternately: and leave the other side alternately until you complete it.
The second type of specific suture, which Gale nus mentioned.
This his speech has been narrated, that he cuts it according to the similarity, by which some of the physicians do it, so that they join every part to its corresponding comparable part by nature: and they apply the end of the sifac to its other end, and the end of the mirach to its other end. And this is done according to what I tell you.
You must fix the needle in the end of the mirach nearest to you from the outer side, and make it penetrate to the inner side at that spot: and leave the two ends of the sifac. Then turn the needle and make it penetrate from the outer side to the inner side at both ends of the sifac, that is, on both sides.
Then turn both, also make both penetrate from the inner to the outer side at the two ends of the mirach which are on the opposite side.
And this method of suturing is better than the common easy suturing, and it is a suturing that has been previously mentioned.
This is therefore the teaching of Galen as well.
And certain people said. The abdominal suture is corrected with two needles. This is to insert one thread into both of them: and begin with the insertion of the needle, from the part that is nearest to you, and make it penetrate all the way to the other side, according to the suturing of those who sew skins equally.
And know that when there is a rupture in the middle of the abdomen: then its suture is more difficult than that of the other parts of the abdomen.
The judgment of the treatment of a wound is the judgment of the other wounds.
Which is because when you encounter a fresh wound with its blood before the air alters it: and you reduce the intestine, and you place it back in its own place, and you adjust it: then apply the powder of carnification on it.
Which if the air has already altered the wound: then apply some ointments that are available to you until they produce pus: and let the threads fall out, and the tissue consolidate and heal. Then care for it as you would the treatment of other wounds until it is healed.
If the medicines are not available to you, then apply old dung on it immediately when it starts to emit pus: and change it twice a day, as I have taught you, until it is healed.
For you do not need other treatment in most cases when wounds are simple.
If you fear that the wound communicates with the principal members in the injury, then it is necessary to soak a soft wool in oil of moderate heat, or in rose oil: and place it around the areas between the groin, and under the armpits.
If it feels pain, or pricking, or putrefaction in its intestines (for this often happens), then administer an enema with astringent, black, warm wine: especially if the putrefaction has already reached the intestine and has caused a discharge penetrating to its cavity.
And you shall know that which is from the large intestine is of easier healing: and that which is from the small intestine is of harder healing.
And the intestine which is called the jejunum does not accept healing from a wound that happens in it at all: and this is because of the multitude of its veins, and the size of them, and because of the subtlety of its body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
If what proceeds from the wound is the cecum, and you encounter it fresh: reduce it according to your method of reduction, by which you equally reduce intestines.
If however time has passed, and it has already become green or black: then it is necessary to tie it with a thread above the place which has turned black from it, so that blood flow does not occur. For in the cecum there are veins and arteries.
Then cut what is beyond that ligament, and place the two ends of the thread hanging from the lower part of the wound outside it: so that the pulling of it is eased for you, and its extraction in the case of the cecum, and the discharge of pus from the wound.
Reminder of the wound that occurs in the intestine.
When a rupture occurs in the intestine and it is small: then it is possible for it to be restored in some people: therefore, because I have seen one who was wounded in his abdomen with a lance strike, and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and the wound was old: and a fistula formed, and excretions and flatulence came out from it.
I therefore applied treatment until I was not confident in his healing: nor did I cease to refine it until he was healed, and the place was strengthened.
After I saw the place already strengthened, I was afraid for the patient, that a harmful accident might occur in his stomach: and that harmful accident did not happen to him. And he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking, and having intercourse, and he entered the bath, and exercised in his diets.
And some of the experiencers have already said that when a wound occurs in the intestine and it is small, then it must be tied according to this method. And it is that you take ants with large heads. Then bring together the two lips of the wound, and place one of the ants that have an open mouth over the two lips of the wound. When it bites on them and closes its mouth, cut off its head, for it adheres and does not loosen.
Then place another ant near the first one, and do not cease to do this with each ant after the other according to the size of the entire wound.
Then reduce it, and sew the wound. For those heads remain attached to the intestine until the intestine is fed and healed, and no harm occurs to the patient thoroughly.
And it is now possible to suture the intestine even with a fine thread: which is taken from the intestine of an animal, attached to it after being inserted into a needle.
And it is that you take the end of this thread from the intestine, and it should be cleaned a lot. Then tie a fine linen thread wound around its end. Then insert that thread into the needle, and sew with it the intestine. Then replace it in the incision.
And this method of suturing with ants and intestine is not unless according to the way of confidence and hope.
Know, a wound that is large, wide, especially if it is in one of the thin intestines: then there is no remedy except for thinning, nor is its healing at all.
Regarding the treatment of Zenichen and fistulas.
Know, that any wound or abscess when it becomes old and antiquated, and turns into an ulcer, and does not consolidate, and always emits pus, and does not heal: then it is generally called a fistula wherever it may be in the body, and we name it Zuchemen.
And the fistula indeed is according to truth a filtered knot, hard, white: with which there is no pain, and it has the concavity of a bird's feather: and because of this some name it Risati, that is, feather.
And at certain times it is moist, emitting pus. And perhaps the moisture splits at certain times. And sometimes this moisture is much, and it is little: and it is thick, and it is thin.
And I have already premised in the division, then when I said wounds, that any ulcer which does not heal, nor flesh is born in it, is not so except for one of nine causes.
One of which is either due to the lack of blood in the body: or due to its malignancy: or because there is hard flesh between it and its lips, preventing the birth of flesh: or because it is full of filth and dirtiness: or because the ulcer itself is putrid, and the matter discharged by it is of bad quality: or because the medicine used for its cure is inappropriate: or because the corruption falling in the region is a kind of pestilence, or due to the nature of the region, as happens in Caesaraugusta: where the digestion of illnesses is difficult, and the healing of abscesses is delayed by nature: or because there is one bone or a number of bones in it.
And I have already shown all these causes and their signs, and their cures with medicines in the division: and it is necessary here that I make you know the cure of Fistula and Zen, which is done by way of operation with the hand.
Know therefore, that Fistula occurs in all parts of the body. For from these are the Fistulas that reach the large veins and arteries, or nerves, or liver: or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs: or to any of the vertebrae of the back, or to any of the composite joints: such as the hand, and foot: and from these are those that go to the proximity of the main member, and similars.
Which therefore of these Fistulas is according to this method, is among diseases difficult to heal, and does not receive cure, and occupation with it is labor and ignorance.
If there is any Fistula whose depth does not reach the places I mentioned: and you hope, and trust in its cure, and wish to understand it, then take a probe of metal or iron, if the Fistula extends straight, and explore it with it.
If there is tortuosity in the Fistula, then investigate it with a fine lead probe. Because lead, with the softness of its body, is lightened and curved around the tortuosity.
If the Fistula has many openings, it is not possible for you to indicate on it with a probe. Therefore, irrigate one of its openings from its openings.
For the moisture with which you irrigate it goes towards the other openings and runs out from them.
Then carefully inquire according to the way that is possible for you: to know whether there is a bone or nerve, and whether the Fistula's depth is far or near: or whether it is one Fistula with many openings, and examine all of it with your utmost strength: with your questioning of the patient, and by finding pain upon pressing with your hand on the area, and similar indications and causes resulting in abscess.
Therefore, when you have stood on all those true examinations, then proceed to the cure with confidence: and it is, that you should consider then if the Fistula is near and apparent, or in a safe place far from the joint, or from the nerve, or artery, or vein, or one of the places I mentioned to you: then cut the Fistula according to what has been previously stated in my narration, and remove what is in it from filtration, and corrupted flesh, which grows at its opening from the flesh, or gland, and similar things: and cure it until it heals.
If however the fistula is of great depth, and is straight: then it is necessary to cut it deeply as much as possible for you. Then clean it from all its corrupted flesh.
Then apply licinia wrapped in sharp medicines: and insert it until the depth of the fistula which you identified with the iron: do this several times with it, until the sharp medicine corrodes all that remains in the depth of the fistula from the corruption.
Then restore it with ointments that generate healthy flesh until it is healed.
If however it does not heal by this method, then cauterize it as we have described.
If therefore the cause of the fistula is a bone, and it is confirmed to you: then investigate it, and cut it as I have told you: unless something prohibits you from doing so by a vein, or nerve, or principal member, as we have said.
If therefore the bone is revealed to you, and there is something of corruption and blackness in it: then scrape it until all its corruption is removed. Then treat it with what causes it to flesh over, until it is healed.
If it does not heal, and discharges pus as it did before: then you know that you have not reached the complete eradication of the corruption.
Reveal it again, and thoroughly examine it, and clean it with all your strength.
Then restore it. If it is healed, that is good: and if not, then you know that that corruption is in a deep part of the body, which you have not reached. Therefore, you have no ingenuity in it, unless to leave it to nature.
If a small bone is corrupted and it is possible for you, draw it out with fine forceps that are suitable for it.
If there are many bones, then carefully make the extraction of all of them, and do not leave anything of them with your strength.
If something from the humors opposes you, and there is no fear or mistake in cutting them: then cut those humors and flesh, if they are there, and free the bones.
If you do not have the preparation for removing bones at your time, then apply something to the wound that will cause it to rot: and leave it until what surrounds those bones from flesh and humors putrefies.
And guard the wound so that it does not heal over. And let the incision which you made in your operation be constricted. Rather place on it, if you fear, tow soaked in ground sulfur with oil: or tow soaked in Egyptian ointment, or some green ointments.
For when those humors rot and the bones separate from them, the removal of them is alleviated, and their extraction is eased.
If however it is one large bone, like the bone of the leg, or the bone of the hip, and similar to those, and what is corrupted from it, is a large part: then scrape it thoroughly until that blackness and corruption are removed. Then restore the wound.
If however what is corrupted in it is a large part, and the corruption has already reached the marrow of the bone, then it is necessary to saw it, and cut it entirely until the place where the corruption reaches: then care for it until it consolidates.
And I tell you of an example that happened to a man in his leg: so that you may set it as an example and aid for your operation.
There was a man of about thirty years of age, to whom pain occurred in his leg, caused by something that moved inside his body, that is, from within, until the matter reached the leg and swelled into a large abscess: and he did not have an external cause.
Therefore, time was wasted with the errors of the physicians until the abscess was opened, and a great deal of matter came out with it. And his treatment was delayed until the leg became fistulated, and many openings were formed in it: which all discharged pus and bodily fluids.
Therefore, he was treated by a multitude of physicians for about two years, and there was no skilled hand in the art until I was called, and I saw his leg, and the matter flowing from those openings in great abundance: moreover, the whole body of the man had already wasted away, and his color was yellow.
I inserted the probe into one of the openings, and the probe reached the mouth.
